Read the passage in <A> and examine the teaching procedure in <B>.Then follow the directions. [3 points]AProcessing instruction, a type of focus-on-form instruction, is basedon the assumption that when processing input, L2 learners havedifficulty in attending to form and meaning at the same time due toworking memory limitations. Not surprisingly, they tend to give priorityto meaning and tend not to notice details of form. Processing instructionuses several principles to explain what learners attend to in the inputand why. Below are some of these principles.The Lexical Preference Principle: In (1), both -es and boy conveythe same information, ‘the third person singular’. Yet, learners prefer tofocus on the lexical item, boy, to arrive at meaning, and often ignorethe grammatical item, -es, while processing the sentence.(1) The boy studies in the library, not at home.The First Noun Principle: Learners tend to process the first noun orpronoun they encounter in a sentence as the agent of action. For example,they may misinterpret (2) as “Jack collected the data for the project.”(2) Jack let Joe collect the data for the project.The Event Possibilities Principle: Event possibilities refer to thelikelihood of one noun being the agent of action as opposed to another.Since it is more likely in the real world that a dog would bite a manthan the other way around, learners would likely misinterpret (3) as “Thedog bit the farmer.”(3) The dog was bitten by the farmer.In processing instruction, teachers provide students with structuredinput activities, taking into consideration the principles above. In astructured input activity, students are forced to attend to form in orderto comprehend a sentence.Teaching Procedure1. Explicit ExplanationExplain how a past tense sentence is constructed in English. Theninform students of why they tend not to notice the past tense marker-ed and thus misinterpret past tense sentences.2. Structured Input ActivityHave students read six sentences and decide whether they describe |an activity that was done in the past or usually happens in the |.present. Then, check the answers together.(1) They watched television at night.(2) They watch television at night.(3) I walk to school on Mondays.(4) | walked to school on Mondays.(5) We played soccer on weekends.(6) We play soccer on weekends.ᄆᄆᄆᄆᄆᄆᄆᄆᄆᄆᄆᄆIdentify the principle in <A> that the teaching procedure in <B> focuseson. Then explain how the structured input activity in <B> helps studentscorrectly process the target form for meaning.| Answer | The structured input activity in <B> is based on the Lexical PreferencePrinciple. In this activity, students are exposed to the pairs of sentencesin the activity, in which each pair has the same lexical meaning butdifferent tenses. Thus, it requires them to focus on the lexical meaningfirst and the form (the past tense marker -ed) second. In other words,through a form-meaning relationship in this activity, they distinguishthe present from the past tense by noticing the past tense marker ‘-ed,’resulting in naturally processing it.서술형에관한전략과유사 하나, 논야하므로기본적인글쓰기에대한형a에 as영은 well-paragraphed writingo] 대한고려가주어식을익히고보다꼼꼼한 017600008 에대한분석에근거 하여, 정보를조직화하도록하는연습을하도록 한다. 따라서기본강좌를 익히고, 실제atr교실수업에대한데이터를분석하도록하는원서강독까지진행한 후, 해당자료나학습상황에대한특징이나문제점등을이끌어내글로표현해보고해결책을제시하는글을써보도록 한다.iV ovens 기줄문제 : 논술형02. Teaching Reading26AVS] Z|] 0] (Schema Theory)o] 따르면인간의사전 경험, 사전지식은그와새로운 BAU 지식을이해하는데관여함으로써새로운지식을받아들이는데끼친다.of celakswtlo |%Schema theory is based on the notion that past experiences lead to thecreation of mental frameworks that help us make sense of new experiences.That is, prior knowledge and expectations that we bring to any situationare based on our background, education, and life experiences shapes ourexpectations and understanding of what we hear or read.01) Content schemata : include general world knowledge, sociocultural knowledge,and topic knowledge.@) Formal schemata : consist of knowledge(rhetorical, discourse structure) wehave of the overall structure of some speech event.Ex, ‘Once upon a time’ herald a certain kind of story which is likely to havea description of characters, and event, and outcome, and possibly amoral comment.Build-up 영어교육론Sana aaaLS(02) Teaching Listening1. Types of Talks(1) Interactional촉진시키기위한대화 로, message 그자체보다화자와화자들간의(01) social type talk(2) person oriented(3) the establishment and maintenance of cordial social relationshipEx, making small talk with a coworker or talking to a friend about aconcern at home(2) Transactional전달하는내용에 ASS 요하는사실적 정보, 명제 SS 전달하기위한대화로 ,실생활에서언어행위의결과를유도 한다.(01) business type talk(2) message oriented@ the focus on content and conveying factual or propositional informationEx. giving instructions, explaining, describing, giving directions, ordering,inquiring, requesting, relating, checking on the correctness of details,verifying understanding(3) Implications for instruction@ Teachers need to provide practice experiences in both transactional talkand interactional talk.@ Students need instruction and listening practice to help them recognizewhen one of the two functions is operating and how they can respondappropriately.Chapter 01 Receptive Skills 2728rus |Types of Input1, Roughly—tuned inputPractical English Language TeachingRoughly tuned input is only approximately at the students’ level; it permitsthem to understand the message although there may be many aspects ofthis message that elude comprehension. An example of roughly-tuned inputmight be a teacher telling the students a story. Here, the features in italicsmay be beyond an intermediate students’ production, but the whole passageis comprehensible.“Well, I read something in the paper the otber day on a very similar theme,basically looking at which cities are the best to live in. Jt took into accountvarious criteria, such as cost of living, safety, education, transport system, andso 072. And 1 think it came up with a list of about twenty, and of these, fivewere in Switzerland’.2. Finely~tuned inputFinely-tuned input is more carefully controlled. It doesn’t contain complexgrammatical constructions or vocabulary far beyond the students’ current level,and is designed so as not to distract the students from the target grammar/vocabulary. In some cases, finely-tuned input may contain only structures andvocabulary that the students have already covered on the syllabus. Here is anexample of finely-tuned input for a low-intermediate class:‘So, [ used to work in Belgium, in Brussels, actually. And I used to travel towork by car, ‘cos I used to have a Ford.... you know a Ford, a type of... make ofcar? And it used to take me about, about twenty minutes to get to work. OK?’The passage above is designed to present ‘used to’.In practice, students benefit from a combination of roughly-tuned and finely-tuned input, the one for more natural examples of language use, the other toprovide crystal clear examples of target grammar.Build-up 영어교육론 12. Comprehension Process우리는 FANS 들을때대부분들리는 text] 메시지를파악하기위해여러전략들을사용한 다. 이를테면어떤이는작은나무들을중심으로파악하는가 하면,어떤이들은전체 eS 파악하기도 한다. 이두가지방식을 60\600 ᄆ - ᅮ 42 과 top—down°]2} 일컨는 다.(1) Bottom—up processing상향식처리과정으로서외부의 자료, 즉듣게되는자료에근거해서 messager도달하는과정을의미 한다. 말을분석해서어휘를찾아내 고, 단어나구문을분석함으로써전체의미를이해하는과정 이다.01) Listeners build understanding by staring with the smallest units of theacoustic message: individual sounds, or phonemes. These are thencombined into words, which, in turn, together make up phrases, clauses,and sentence. Finally, individual sentences combine to create ideas andconcepts and relationships between them.@) The process in a linear one, in which meaning itself is derived as the laststep in the process.(3) Examples(@) Listen to the teacher reading pairs for word. Each pair differs by onesound. Listening Strategies(1) Listening for global understanding~—gist@ Objective : to give learners practice in understanding only the main ideasof a passage. It is not always necessary for us to understand the details ofwhat we listen to.(2) Tasks(a) Listen and answer true/false, yes-no, or open-ended questions aboutthe main ideas of the passage.(6) Provide a list of statements and check off those that reflect the main ideas.©) Choose a picture that corresponds to the main idea of the text.(3) ExamplesIs the speaker describing a vacation or a day in the office?090 Is the radio report about news or weather?(©) Why is the speaker asking the man questions?@ Did the speaker like or dislike the movie?34 Build-up 영어교육론(2) Listening for specific information—scanning@ Objective : to give learners practice in picking out specific information in atext without expecting them to understand every word.(2) Tasks(@) Jigsaw task in which different groups listen for different information;exchange information in new groups(6) Fill in missing words/numbers in a text.©) Provide a list of specific information and check off those ideas that areheard.@ Listen and point to pictures/words as they appear in the passage.©) Order information as it appears in the text using pictures or words.0) Choose the correct word, number, etc.(multiple choice)® Correct misinformation in a text.09 Fill in a grid/table with words or draw pictures.(3) Examples(@) How much did they say the tickets cost?(b) Did the speaker’s husband say he picked up the kids?©) Why did the speaker say he was studying Chinese?@) Where did she say the meeting was being held?(3) Listening for detail0) Objective : to practice listening intensively for details of the text. Learnersmove form identifying short, factual information to interpreting themeaning more deeply.@) Task : The types of activities are similar to the ones of listening for gistand specific information. Difference is the content of the questions.Listening for specific information with news headlines might entail simplyidentifying the countries mentioned and the event that occurred in eachone. A more detailed listening could require learners to identify theplayers, the time, or the exact location of the events.Chapter 01 Receptive Skills 35Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3 0688Practical English Language Teaching(4) Making inference@ Objective : to give learners practice in analyzing, interpreting, and evaluatingthe meaning of a text. Intermediate to advanced-level students need practicewith making inferences and going beyond the factual information presentedto them.(2) Tasks(8) Discuss underlying messages e.g. view advertisements and determinethe target audience for the ad.(6) Problem-solving or decision-making activities.(©) Choose statements that could be inferred from the listening passage(multiple choice or true/false statements).(3) Example : What are the speakers implying by what they said?(5) Listening to confirm predictions—monitoring@ Objective : to enable leaners to confirm predictions made during pre-listening, to pay attention to what they are understanding and what theyare missing.(2) Tasks(@) Match predictions with what’s heard.060) Check answers to pre-listening activities.(6) Predicting@ Objective : to generate the learners’ schemata. Pre-listening tasks serve toget the learners think about and talk about the content of what they areabout to hear. This will enable them to anticipate content and facilitatecomprehension of the listening passage.36 Build-up 영어교육론재ly In the Classroom1. Extensive vs. Intensive Listening(1) Extensive listening담화내용의전체적인의미의이해=we자신이 SS 자료를선택하며교실수업상황밖에서 이루어진다.(01) Teachers encourage students to choose for themselves what they listen toand to do for pleasure and general language improvement.@) Extensive listening usually takes place outside the classroom.(3) Students listen a lot of easy materials with a minimal task or no task at all.@ Materials for extensive listening can be obtained from a number of sources:cassette or CD, broadcasts online, etc.© It is useful for increasing motivation, listening, pronunciation, and goodspeaking habits.AQ Build-up 영어교육론끄Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) ;(2) Intensive listening담화 USS 바탕으로특정한정보를찾거나언어자질에대한학습을목적으로수업상황에서이루어지는듣기활동을 말한다.에rr@® It allows students the opportunity to focus on discrete points of the languageand to develop listening skills.@) Intensive listening usually takes place in the classroom with teachers’preparation.(03) It can include replaying a tape several times, which encourages studentsto get as much information as, is necessary or appropriate from a singlehearing.=e Further readingTypes of classroom listening performance1. ReactiveSometimes you want a learner simply to listen to the surface structureof and utterance for the sole purpose of repeating it back to you. Whilethis kind of listening performance requires little meaningful processing,it nevertheless may be a legitimate, even though a minor, aspect of aninteractive, communicative classroom. This role of the listener as merelya “tape recorder” is very limited because the listener is not generatingmeaning. About the only role that reactive listening can play in aninteractive classroom is in brief choral or individual drills that focus onpronunciation.2. IntensiveTechniques whose only purpose is to focus on components (phonemes,words, intonation, discourse markers, etc.) of discourse may be consideredto be intensive—as opposed to extensive—in their requirement thatstudents single out certain elements of spoken language.Chapter 01 Receptive Skills 41PartPractical English Language Teaching3. ResponsiveA significant proportion of classroom listening activity consists of shortstretches of teacher language designed to elicit immediate responses. Thestudents’ task in such listening is to process the teacher talk immediatelyand to fashion an appropriate reply.4. SelectiveIn longer stretches of discourse such as monologues of a couple of minutesof considerably longer, the task of the student is not to process everything thatwas said, but rather to scan the material selectively for certain information. Thepurpose of such performance is not to look for global or general meanings,necessarily, but to be able to find important information in a field of potentiallydistracting information. Selective listening differs from intensive listening in thatthe discourse is in relatively long lengths.5. ExtensiveThis sort of performance, unlike the intensive processing describedabove, amis to develop a top-down, global understanding of spokenlanguage. Extensive performance could range from listening to lengthylectures, to listening to a conversation and deriving a comprehensivemessage or purpose.6. InteractiveInteractive listening performance can include all five of the above typesas learners actively participate in discussions, debates, conversations, roleplays, and other pair and group work. Their listening performance mustbe intricately integrated with speaking (and perhaps other) skills in theauthentic give and take of communicative interchange.42 Build-up SO2S= I5. Forexample, if learners give a wrong answer to a written comprehensionquestion, it may be because they have not understood the question(reading) or because they cannot formulate an answer (writing) ratherthan because their listening is at fault. Conversing : 들은내용을토대로대화에참여하기(3) Post-listening(=7| 후 단계)들은내용을바르게이해했는지확인하거나들은 USS 말하기, 읽기등다른기능으로통합하여듣기 HAS 마무리 한다.0) 목적 : to give learners further practice using the content of the text, tofurther check understanding of the text through another medium.@) Post-listening activities can take students into a more intensive phase ofstudy in which aspects of bottom-up listening are practised.09 It can involve integration with other skills through development thetopic into reading, speaking, or writing activities.© The whole class checks answers to pre-set questions and responds tothe content of the passage.We focus on the product of listening when we should be interested in theprocess—what is going on in the heads of our learners. Wrong answers aremore informative than right ones; it makes sense to spend time finding outwhere and how understanding broke down. On this view, the main aim of a48 Build-up SojwS= 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers &listening lesson is diagnostic: identifying listening problems and putting themright. Armed with evidence of why a misunderstanding occurred, teacherscan design remedial microlistening exercises which tackle the cause of theproblem. Here, dictation is a particularly useful tool. Suppose that learnersfind it difficult to recognize weak forms. A series of sentences can be dictatedcontaining examples of the weak forms, to ensure that students interpretthem correctly the next time they encounter them.Remedial exercises should not be restricted to low-level skills such asword recognition; they can also be used to develop higher-level ones(distinguishing important pieces of information, anticipating, noticing topicmarkers, and so on.)A diagnostic aim for the listening lesson implies a change in lesson shape.Instead of the kind of long pre-listening period which some teachers employ,it is much more fruitful to allow time for an extended post-listening period inwhich learners’ problems can be identified and tackled.(2) 활동(@) Checking listeners’ comprehension00 Summarizing : 교사가단순히배운내용을 AES 통해서요약하도록요구할수있지만 group summary, take it in turns, note comparison 등다양한방식의요약활동이가능하 다.© Discussion : 듣기활동의내용에초점을두어파트너혹은그룹내에서토론활동을함으로써듣기와말하기의통합수업모형의교실기법을수행할수있다.Chapter 01 Receptive Skills 49PartPractical English Language Teaching|*Before You ListenWork with your partner. Listening Performance(1) Dictogloss들은내용을바탕으로이야기를재구성하도록하는 dictogloss BES 상향식듣기과정과하향식듣기과정을모두 Bee 하는대표적인통합형과제 (1016881176task)°] TH,@ The dictogloss technique provides a useful bridge between bottom-up andtop-down listening.(2) In the dictogloss activity, learners listen to a short text read twice to themwhile they take notes. In this stage, they are primarily concerned withidentifying individual elements in the text (> bottom-up strategy).@ During the small group discussions, they reconstruct a written form of thetext from these note (— top-down strategy).©) Required Steps for a Dictogloss Activity* Vocabulary study activities to prepare for the text.1. Reading Approach(1) Bottom-up approach} 향식접근법은철자에서시작해서 단어, 문장, 텍스트전체의의미를파악하는Ft 개Bottom-up approaches that rely heavily on decoding letters, words, andsentences are one-way approaches to reading.* Students start with the fundamental basics of letter and sound recognition,followed by word recognition.* They build up to the identification of grammatical structures, sentences,and longer texts.* Letters, letter clusters, words, phrases, sentences, longer text, and finallymeaning is the order in achieving comprehension.@ Sight wordsThe learner relies on visual memory to match sound with writing. Sightwords are high-frequency words students can recognize on sight withouthaving to decode the letters. The, all, an and J are all sight words. Somesight words are especially difficult to sound out or decode because theydo not follow regular spelling patterns—right, there, look, and should.58 Build-up 영어교육론 II(2) Phonics approachA phonics approach generally emphasizes teaching children to whichindividual letters of the alphabet with their specific English pronunciation.Phonics, then, generally involves teaching students the sound-letterrelationships used in reading and writing.(3) A linguistic approachIt exposes children to certain carefully selected words containing regularspelling patterns so that they can infer the letter-sound relationships inthose words. For example, similar looking words groups such as take—bake—lake—cake and common rhyme or word-ending patterns such as—ate, —ell, or —ight are used to teach the sound pattern.(0) A basal approach (= A graded reader approach)The teacher helps children to read through careful control andsequencing of the language and the sounds that they are exposed to. Asa result, basal readers are carefully graded, sequenced to present sounds,vocabulary, and individual skills at increasing levels of difficulty andalso to provide carefully controlled practice, recycling, and testing of thelanguage and skills.(2) Top-down approach향식접근법은 text] 언어적자료외에독자가지닌배경지식을이용하여전체저의미를먼저파악하는접근방식을 말한다.Holistic, top-down approaches begin with the idea that comprehensionresides in the reader.ᆞ The reader uses background knowledge, makes predictions, and searchesthe text to confirm or reject the predictions that are made.* A passage can thus be understood even if all of the individual words arenot understood.* Within a top-down approach to reading the teacher should focus onmeaning generating activities rather than on mastery of word recognition.Chapter 01 Receptive Skills 59Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 22) aPart60Practical English Language Teaching@ The language experience approachIn the language experience approach (LEA) students need to dictate thestories orally and collaboratively in order to make their reading materialsbased on their own experiences. LEA allows students to see a direct linkbetween oral and written language. Because the children have composedthe stories themselves, there is a close match between their knowledge orexperience and the texts they read.ly In the Classroom+ Stage 1The students of class dictate a “story” usually based upon anexperience they have had, that the teacher writes down on a largesheet of paper. The teacher tries to maintain the extra wording andexpressions that the children have dictated Gf it contains errors, thechildren can correct them later as their proficiency increases).ᆞ Stage 2The teacher then either reads the story to the class Gf the childrenare beginning readers), or has the class read back the story they havecomposed, providing any help they need along the way to figure outindividual words.* Stage 3Depending on their level of ability and needs, the class will thenengage in various extended activities based upon the original story,including focusing on individual words, letters. or meanings of variousnoteworthy parts.* Stage 4Ultimately, the children are expected to move from the stories theyhave dictated toward being able to read those written by others.Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers a3i,20(2) Literature-based approachIt uses children’s literature with the intention of focusing on meaning,interest, and enjoyment. In this approach, they often select their ownbooks and read them on their own or with others. Books are used whichcontain authentic language, thus, it greatly facilitates students’ success andskill development.@ Whole language approachIn a meaning based approach or a whole language approach, studentswork from attempting first to understand the meaning of the overall textbefore they work in the linguistic forms comprising it. The focus shouldbe on meaning and keeping the language whole, as opposed to breakingit down into smaller units as in the bottom-up approach.3. Extensive vs. intensive Reading(1) Extensive reading다양한텍스트혹은보다긴텍스트를즐거움과전반적인내용의이해읽기활동으로대부분교실밖의실생활 (7681-1148/ 에서 이루어진다.001위해읽는ᆞ means reading many books or longer text without a focus on classroomexercises.* It does not aim to test comprehension skills.ᆞ The teacher encourages students to choose for themselves what they readand to do so for pleasure and general language improvement.* Read the text fluently and fast for entertainment and general understandingbut without such careful attention to the details.* The more someone read, the more they pick up vocabulary and grammarfrom the texts without realizing it.Chapter 01 Receptive Skills 61PartPractical English Language Teaching(2) Intensive reading특정텍스트의정확한이해혹은읽기기능- ᄀ 7 로[ 요습을위해교실수업에서행해지는읽기활동1 involves textbook activities to develop comprehension or a particularreading skill.* Read the texts closely and carefully with the intention of gaining anunderstanding of as much detail as possible.* It involves approaching the guidance of a teacher to enable students todevelop specific receptive skills.« It is often teacher-chosen and directed.* The aim is to arrive at an understanding, not only of what the text means,but of how the meaning is produced.Pus |Types of Classroom Reading PerformanceClassroom Reading PerformanceIntensive Extensive——_ | ~Linguistic Content Skimming . They stole the gold and otherdom, the Middle Kingdom, and the New treasures and destroyed the pharaoh’s body.Kingdom. These are further divided into 35 Consequently, sculptors began to create5 dynasties.A dynasty was a period when a single statues of the pharaoh, such as the portrait offamily provided a succession of rulers. When Khafre on his throne.They put these statuesone pharaoh died, a successor was chosen inside the tomb so that the ka could enterfrom the same family.It was important to keep this stone statue for the journey to the nextthe blood ofa royal family pure;therefore,the 40 world.10 Pharaoh was not allowed to marry outside ofthe immediate family.The Old KingdomThe earliest dynastic period began around3100 BC when Upper and Lower Egyptwere united by a powerful pharaoh named15 Menes. Menes established his capital atMemphis and founded the first of the thirtyone Egyptian dynasties.It was during the Old Kingdom thatthe pyramids were built. These massive20 tombs were an attempt to keep the bodyof the pharaoh safe.The Egyptians believedthat the soul, or ka, remained with the bodyuntil death. At death, the ka left the bodyfor a time, but it later returned and united25 with the body again for the journey to thenext world. If the body was destroyed, theka had to travel aimlessly for all eternity. Forthis reason, the Egyptians went to greatlengths to protect the body—especially the30 body of the pharaoh, for he was both a king 2and, in the eyes of the people, a god. Read the passage and fill in the blank with ONE or TWO words.Listening scriptA: Let’s go outside. We could go for a walk. Maybe play tennis.B: Look out the window. It’s raining.A: Raining. Oh, no.One of common types of listening exercise is listening for,This often involves tasks such as identifying main ideas, noting asequence of events and the like. In the above dialogue, it could involvea very general question such as, “What's the main topic?” or, if moretask support is needed, giving the learners a few choices (friends,sports, the weather) and having them choose the main topic.| Your answer |Chapter 01 Receptive Skills 83PartPractical English Language Teaching02. Read the passage and complete the blank with EIGHT words by using thegiven words. You can use one given word more than once.In pedagogical terms, it is possible to draw a distinction betweenbottom-up and top-down approaches to listening comprehension.Bottom-up listening activities focus learner on the individual elementsand building blocks of the language. Decoding oral utterances,discriminating between individual sounds, in particular those withminimal contrasts and identifying different stress, rhythm and intonationpatterns feature prominently in the early stages of learning, and thestudent is only gradually moved . Ina listening comprehension course, the assumption that learning is agradual, linear and additive process is evident in the way the inputis staged. While bottom-up processing is evoked from sounds top-down processing is evoked from a bank of prior knowledge and globalexpectations and other background information that the listener bringsto the text. In this sense, with low-level learners who would clearly bechallenged by such input, the difficulty can be minimized by lettingthem hear the text as often as necessary and providing a range ofactivities of increasing complexity. The first time they hear the text, theymight be asked to identify how many speakers they hear. The secondtime they hear the text, they can be given a list of key words. Next, theycan be given phrases to identify. Lastly, they can be asked to identifythe number of questions they hear.| from, to, text, word, sound, sentence84 Build-up 40282 11Guideline for Pre-service Teachers gs) yo03. Approach to Speaking1970 년대중반 이후, 언어능력이라는것이단순히문법지식을측정하는시험을통과하는 SAS 의미하는것이아니라다른사람들과상호작용을할수있는의사소통 SES 의미하는보다넓은개념으로확대 되었다.In the mid-1970s the notion of linguistic competence came to be viewed asa component of the broader ideas of communicative competence “the abilityof language learners to interact with other speakers, to make meaning, asdistinct from their ability to perform on discrete-point tests of grammaticalknowledge”. Being communicatively competent “requires an understandingof sociocultural contexts of language use”.@ Sociolinguistic competence : This involves register (degrees of formalityand informality), appropriate word choice, style shifting, and politenessstrategies.(2) Strategic competence : In terms of speaking, this is the learner’s ability touse language strategies to compensate for gaps in skills and knowledge.For example, if you don’t know a word you need to express yourmeaning, what strategies can you use to make your point?03) Discourse competence : “how sentence elements are tied together,” whichincludes both cohesion and coherence. Cohesion is “the grammatical and/or lexical relationship between the different parts of a sentence”. Cohesionincludes reference, repetitions, synonyms, and so on. In contrast,coherence involves “how texts are constructed”.94 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers a(Extract 1 |Jeff: Hey, Linsey, how’s it going?Linsey : Wow! I just had a test and it was really hard!Jeff. : Oh, what was the test about?Linsey : Statistics! All those formulas are so confusing!In this brief conversation, there are several examples of cohesion. In Linsey’sfirst turn the pronoun it refers to the test she has just mentioned. In Jeff's secondturn, he repeats the word test. In Linsey’s second turn, the words statistics andformulas are synonymous. Finally, in Jeffs last turn that stuff refers to statisticsand formulas. All these devices make the conversation cohesive.Coherence also has to do with “the relationships which link the meaningsof utterance in a discourse”. However, coherence often involves the speakers’background knowledge. For example, the following exchange is coherent becausethe two people know that the two events are scheduled at the same time.(Extract 2 |Person 1 : Going to the review session?Person 2 : Rugby practiceBoth cohesion and coherence contribute to discourse competence. For peoplespeaking in a new language, the specific linguistic elements that make speechcohesive can be especially demanding to produce during the pressure of aconversation.2. Characteristics of a Successful Speaking(1) Learner talk a lot,수업시간에학생들이가능한많은발화를 한다.As much as possible of the period of time alloted to the activity is in factoccupied by learner talk. This may seem obvious, but often most time istaken up with teacher talk or pauses.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 95PartPractical English Language Teaching(2) Participation is even,수업시간에가능한모든학생들이참여한 다.Classroom discussion is not dominated by a minority of talkative participants:All get a chance to speak, and contribution are fairly evenly distributed.(3) Motivation is high.학생들은흥미로운주제에관심을 보이며, 적극적으로무엇인가를말을하려고 한다.Learners are eager to speak: because they are interested in the topic andhave something new to say about it.(4) Language is of an acceptable level.학생들은비교적정확한언어를사용 하여, 서로관련있고이해가능한발화를 한다.Learners express themselves in utterances that are relevant, easilycomprehensible to each other, and of an acceptable level.노 220 코 <Why are learners unmotivated?— Lack of success over time/lack of perception of progress~ Uninspired teaching— Boredom— Lack of perceived relevance of materials~ Lack of knowledge about the goals of the instructional program~ Lack of appropriate feedbackWhat can be done?— Make instructional goals explicit to learners— Break learning down into sequences of achievable steps— Link learning to be needs and interests of the learners— Allow learners to bring their own knowledge and perspective into the learningprocess96 Build-up S0jzS=9 ~Guideline for Pre-service Teachers— Encourage creative language use— Help learners to identify the strategies underlying the learning tasks they areengaged in— Develop ways in which learners can record their own progress3. Problems and Solutions(1) Problem 1. Inhibition(XHOKS 보호하기위한방어 기제)> Problem : 학생들은때때로방어기제때문에 2 언어사용에어려움을 겪는다.Learners are often inhibited about trying to say things in a foreign languagein the classroom. Students are* worried about making mistakes* fearful of criticism or losing face* simply shy of the attention that their speech attracts.= Solutions© Use group work : 학생들의방어기제를낮추고발화의기회를더많이제공할수있다.Using group work increases the sheer amount of learner talk going onin a limited period of time and also lowers the inhibitions of learners whoare unwilling to speak in front of the full class.@ Base the activity on easy language : 집중적인언어학습에사용하는언어보다보다쉬운언어를사용하는활동을제공 한다.The level of language needed for a discussion should be lower than thatused in intensive language-learning activities in the same class. It shouldbe easily recalled and produced by the participants, so that they canspeak fluently with the minimum of hesitation.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 97PartPractical English Language Teaching(2) Problem 2. Nothing to say— Problem : 자신이생각하는 AS 표현하고자하는의지가적은학생들이 있다.Some learners complain that they can not think of anything to say: theyhave no motive to express themselves beyond the guilty feeling that theyshould be speaking.— Solution : Make a careful choice of topic and task to stimulate interest.학생들의흥미를자극할수있는다양한 16010 과 taskS 제공 한다. 또한현재진행하고있는과업의목적이보다명확할경우학생들의참여와동기유발이확대 된다.Teachers need to provide various topics and tasks which can draw leaners’attention. On the while, the clearer the purpose of the discussion, the moremotivated participants will be.Problem 3, Low or uneven participation(a)—> Problem : 대단위수업에서학생들은똑같은발화기회를갖지못하기때문에대화에참여하지못하는경우가발생한 다.Only one participant can talk at a time, which means that each one still haveonly very little talking time. This problem is compounded by the tendency ofsome learners to dominate while others speak very little or not at all.— Solution : Give some instruction or training in discussion skills.정하여발화그룹활동이나전체활동에서토론규칙등을루If the task is based on group discussion, then include instructions aboutparticipation when introducing it..Or, appoint a chairperson to each groupwho will regulate participation.(4) Problem 4, Mother—tongue use= Problem : 목표언어를잘구사하지못하거나본인의수준보다높은수준의수업에서학생들은모국어로대화를시도한 다.98 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers as) \In classes where the learners share the same mother tongue, they may tend touse it because it is easier, it feels unnatural to speak to one another in a foreignlanguage and they feel less exposed if they are speaking their mother tongue.= Solution : keep students speaking the target language.상기 시키고, 그룹활동을학생들을계속모니터하면서목표어사용에대한필요성을어떻게이끌어갈것인지에대한보고서를작성하도록 한다. 때로는그룹리더나다른팀원중모니터요원을지정하여모국어사용에대한 BAS 정할수도 있다.Appoint one of the group as monitor, whose job is to remind participantsito use the target language, and perhaps report later to the teacher how wellthe group managed to keep it.Dealing with the Reluctant SpeakerFive Principal factors accounting for the reluctance of students to speak upin class1. Students’ perceived low proficiency in English학생들은 SAAS SSS 가지고있음에도불구하고자신의영어실력을더낮게인지하여영어로말하는것을꺼리게 된다.Videotaped data from secondary school classrooms showed that althoughstudents did have the competence to respond to teachers’ questions in English,their lack of confidence, unwillingness to take risks, and a perception that theirEnglish was poor resulted in a marked reluctance to respond.2. Students’ fear of mistake and derision친구들앞에서실수를하고비웃음을당할 AS 두려워하여말하기를꺼 린다.Students were also afraid of making tools of themselves in front of their peers.In addition, there is a cultural factor that functions in a number of Asian culturesinhibiting students from speaking up in front of their peers.3. Teachers’ intolerance of silence은교사들이침묵에대한인내심이낮아학생들에게충분한시간을주지 않는다:Many of the teachers taking part in the study gave the students little or no waittime.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 99PartPractical English Language Teaching4, Uneven allocation of turns침묵에대한교사의낮은인내심이더잘하는학생들에게말하기기회를더많이주는 Lolo] 되기도 한다.From the data collected in the study it became clear points out, this is probablyrelated to the intolerance of silence. By targeting the better students, teacherscould be sure that there would not be periods of silence or confusion in theirclassrooms.5. Incomprehensible input교사의언어가학생들의이해수준에비해 어렵다.The final factor was the overly difficult teachers’ language input. One teacher,for instance, having viewed herself teaching, reported that, “After viewingmyself asking questions, I realized that what I thought were simple and clearquestions were in fact quite difficult to understand. Principles for Teaching Speaking(1) Basic principles01) Plan speaking tasks that involve negotiation for meaning학습자들이자신의언어를더발전시키고연습할수있는기회를가질수있도록의미협상이수반되는말하기활동을계획 한다.In the process of negotiation for meaning, the language addressed tolearners gets adjusted to their level and becomes comprehensible to them.And as learners work to make themselves understood, they must attendto accuracy. This is, they must select the right vocabulary, apply grammarrules, pronounce words carefully, and so on. In doing so, they may“notice the gap” between what they want to say and what they can say, orbetween what they say and what other people say. By planning speakingtasks that require learners to negotiate for meaning, teachers can givestudents valuable chances for practice and language development.(2) Personalize the content of soeaking activities whenever possible.학습자들이각자의 환경, 흥미, 목표 SS 활용하여말할수있는활동들을계획 한다,Personalization is the process of making activities match the learners’own circumstances, interests, and goals. Personalizing an exercise canbe as simple as using students’ names, academic majors, cities, or jobsin speaking activities. Or you can build role-plays around situationssuggested by the learners. You can also use song lyrics or readingpassages selected by the students or based on their interests as the basisof logic puzzles and picture-based activities. Personalizing languagelessons is partly a matter of careful planning and partly of respondingcreatively to students’ questions and comments during activities.(3) Provide opportunities for learners to notice the gap.학습자들이 ' 자신이말하고싶은것 ' 과 ' 말할수있는 BW 사이에서발생하는차이를인식할수있는기회를제있는 한다.개102 Build-up 영어교육론끄Guideline for Pre-service Teachers @What does it mean to say that learners should be given opportunitiesto “notice the gap?” This phrase describes an experience that learnershave when they are interacting in English. It refers to the learner realizingthat the way he is saying something in the target language differs fromthe way native or proficient speakers say it. This awareness can beabout individual words, grammar rules, idioms, appropriate phrases,pronunciation—any component of the language she is learning. Someresearchers believe that this awareness must occur before a learner canmake the necessary adjustments in her developing competence. The ideasof noticing the gap is not the same as monitoring ones’ own output. Theconcept of monitoring refers to learners checking what they say or write,based on rules they’ve already learned. Monitoring may lead learners tonotice the gap, but this experience can happen in the absence of knownrules. Noticing the gap can involve the learner’s realization that he doesn’tknow the word or the structure he is trying to say. In fact, the phrase“noticing the gap” has also been used with the idea of learners realizingthat there is a differences between what they want to say and whatthey can say. This process involves the development of linguistic self-awareness on the learners’ part. There are many things that we as teacherscan do to help learners become more self-aware.(2) Considering affective factor0) Strong language ego하생들이말하기활동에적극적으로참여하도록하기위해서는약한언어적자아를강하게만들어주어야 한다. O|= inhibitionS “#3! self—confidences 높임으로써(2) High motivation학생들의참여가큰역할을하기때문에그들의흥미와요구를고려한학습활동을제공 한다.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 103PartPractical English Language Teaching(>) Some preconditions for effective motivation* Orderly classroomSupportive ᆞ Teacher is skilled in classroom managementEnvironment * Students are nonanxious, and feel comfortable taking risksᆞ Feedback is positiveAppropriate LevelPpropria Tasks are neither too easy nor too difficultof Difficulty¢ Students know what they are expected to learn and why! * Activities are meaningful and worthwhileMeaningful ; ger 에이이이이Learning * Relationship between objective and activities is clearᆞ Tasks are sequenced so that new tasks build on and extend onesthat come before students are given a reason to be in class* Motivational strategy is matched to instructional needStrategies ᆞ Particular strategies are not overusedᆞ Teacher uses a range of strategies* Students can relate content to own experienceContent . , ,* Topics are interesting(8) Encouraging risk-taking학습자들이 OSS 발생시킴에도불구하고적극적으로말하기활동에참여하는자세가중요하 다. 이를위해서는 meaning (fluency) based activityS 제공하고오류수정은최소화하며 affective classroom atmospheres 형성해야 한다.@ Increasing accomplishment학생들의자신감을증가시키는방법중가장중요한요소는학습과제에대한성취감을중대시키는 것이다. 학습자들의수준을고려하여잠재적인능력안에있는과제를제공하거나여러수준의과제를제공한뒤학습자들이본인에게적합한과제를선택하도록할수 있다.104 © Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers S38) ※-5. Accuracy vs, Fluency정확성초점의연습 See 새로운항목을제시하고해당항목을정확하게표현하도록하면서오류발생시오류를수정해주는 반면, 유창성초점의연습활동은학습자들이알고있는표현을과제를기반으로보다자연스러운의사소통상황에서사용하도록유도한다0) Accuracy practice is intended to establish some correctness in theproduction of new items immediately after they are presented, or tocorrect errors later on. Fluency practice is intended to get the learners touse new items in more natural communication.@) In accuracy practice, learners are usually very aware that they arerepeating the new item over and over again. In fluency practice teachersshould try to get the learners’ attention off the language and onto thecommunication of ideas. Repetition, or repeated use, of the new itemshould be naturally combined with other language in communication.(3) There may be more errors in fluency practice than in accuracy practice,but the teacher should not interrupt learners to correct errors.09)Learner 1 : Have you ever been to Prague?Learner 2 : No, I haven’t. The teacher in Extract 6 uses two-word cues (for example,‘watch-Japan’) every time. The teacher in Extract 7 uses the question pattern‘What about your ? several times, and then moves to the pattern‘Where was your made?On a-scale from unnatural/non-communicative to natural/communicative,Extracts 5, 6, and 7 might be classified something like this:Unnatural/ Natural/non-communicative - communicative108 Build-up SowS= 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers & or»The most unnatural/non-communicative practice is in Extract 6. The teachergets the learners to produce sentences by using the artificial cue ‘object-country’,for example, ‘Watch-Japan’. And she does not learn any new information fromthe learners’ answers. The most natural/communicative practice is in Extract 7.The teacher uses questions as cues, for example, “What about your shoes’and “Where was your pen made?’ She learns real, new information from thelearners’ answers about where their possessions were made. And she respondswith conversational comments, for example, ‘They’re nice’. Extract 5 comessomewhere in between. The teacher uses questions rather than cues, but thereis no variation in them. The learners answer with information known to theteacher, and the teacher makes no conversational comments.6. In the first place there are factors to do with the datathat learners are working with. (How dense/complex are the texts that learnersare required to process? How abstract/concrete is the content in relation to thelearners’ experience? How much contextual support is provided?) The secondset of factors has to do with the task itself.(How many steps are involved in thetask? How relevant and meaningful is the task? How much time is available? Whatdegree of grammatical accuracy is provided? How much assistance is provided?How clearly is the task set up for the learners? How much practice or rehearsal timeis available?) Finally, there are factors that are internal to the speakers themselves.These factors, which are largely outside the teachers’ control, include the level ofconfidence and motivation of the learners, prior knowledge of content, degreeof linguistic knowledge and skill, extent of cultural knowledge, and the degree offamiliarity with the task type itself.Build-up 영어교육론 11Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 33)Factors affecting task difficulty*the degree to which the language event is embedded in a contextthat facilitates comprehension;*the degree to which the language event makes cognitive demandson the learner;* the degree to which background knowledge can be used;ᆞ the amount of assistance provided to the learner;-the complexity of the language that the learner is required toproduce;- the degree of emotional stress involved in completing the task;* the interest and motivation of the learneraly In the Classroom2009 학년도기출Step 1 : Pre-taskThe teacher introduces the lesson content about favorite school subjectsby asking students what subjects they studied at school and makes a liston the board. Students are then asked to classify the subjects into groupcategories. The teacher then tells the class about subjects she liked andhated, and explains why. The teacher then reads the instructions for aspeaking activity: “Tell your partner about the school subjects you like bestand least and explain your reasons.” Before beginning, students are giventhree minutes to write down what they will say in the speaking activity.Chapter 02. Productive Skills111112Practical English Language TeachingStep 2 : Task cycleThe students begin the speaking activity and talk about their schoolsubjects. In the process of completing the activity, the students occasionallystop to think about and discuss language-related problems, i.e. gaps intheir interlanguage knowledge, to resolve their misunderstandings incommunication. After finishing the activity, each student prepares a brieforal presentation about their partner’s favorite subjects. The teacher selectsa few students to present their partner’s answers to the whole class.Step 3 : Follow upAfter presentations, the teacher gives the students a brief written transcriptof two native speakers of English doing the same speaking activity theyjust completed. Individually, the students read the transcript and underlineall the phrases that are used by the native speakers to express ‘likes’and ‘dislikes’ of school subjects. The teacher then reviews these with thestudents. Following this, the teacher has the students find all the examplesof comparatives and superlatives in the transcript and figure out how theydiffer in usage.oly In the Classroom2011 학년도기출Fighting Jet LagPre-task* The teacher shows visual materials related to jet lag and elicits experiencesfrom students.Task Cycle 1* The teacher asks students to brainstorm, in pairs, ways to overcome jet lag.* Pairs select three items from what they have brainstormed.* Pairs rehearse how to explain their choices and then present their list tothe class with justifications.Build-up 영어교육론 11Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) aTask Cycle 2* The teacher distributes copies of a magazine article about overcoming jetlag and has students write down the three ways mentioned in the text.¢ Pairs compare their list to that of the article.« Students decide which pair has the most similar ways.Post-task- Students circle adverbial phrases expressing time and place in themagazine article.* Students complete a grammar worksheet.7. Speaking Activities일반적으로의사소통과업이란한사람은정보를가지고있고다른사람은가지고은경우에진행되는의사교환을의미 한다. 이를 ‘information 887 이라하는데수업중에진행되는이와같은 AAAS 활동은학생들이서로정보를여실제적이고유의미한방식으로상호작용하도록하면서학습한언어를이(1) Information gapIt is a useful activity in which one person has information that the otherlacks. They must use the target language to share that information. Forinstance, one student has the directions to a party and must give them to aclassmate.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 113PartPractical English Language Teaching|? Example | Information gapSpot the differen 은 [0 )@® SPO! le di erences Reward Biemantany | Spot the differences Rewald BlementiryPicture &(2) Jigsaw activitiesThese are a bidirectional or multidirectional information gap. Eachperson in a pair or group has some information the other persons need.For example, one student could have a timetable for train travel in Canada.Another could have a map of Canada. Without showing each other the visualinformation, they must speak English to plan a one-week trip.114 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers Ss) ᅵ|In the Classroom2010 학년도기출You Are a Witness!(1) The teacher prepares a set of four picture cards showing the story ofa minor car accident. She divides the class into four groups, with fourstudents in each group. She tells the class that they are going to witnessa car accident, but that they can see only one card.(2) The teacher flashes one picture card to each group for a few secondsonly. Then she asks the members of each group to discuss and agree onwhat they have just seen.(3) The teacher assigns each member of each group a number: 1, 2, 3, and4, Then she re-groups students as follows:[1234 (1234 | 1234) 1234 > 1111) 2222) 3333 | 4444](4) The teacher asks the members of the new groups to describe what eachperson saw and to decide on the sequence of the accident.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 115hitpynnn fae개 {PartPractical English Language Teaching(3) Role—playsThese are also excellent activities for speaking in the relatively safeenvironment of the classroom. In a role-play, students are given particularroles in the target language. For example, one student plays a touristtelephoning the police to report his wallet stolen. The other plays the role ofa police officer trying to help the tourist file a report. Role-plays give learnerspractice speaking the target language before they must do so in a realenvironment.(4) SimulationsThese are more elaborate than role-plays. In a simulation, props anddocuments provide a somewhat realistic environment for language practice.So for instance, in a language lesson about the grocery store, a teacher mightbring in “products” for the students to buy and even play money for makingtheir purchases. A check-out counter would be set up for the students topractice transactional speaking with the cashier.116Laas,1. Prabhu2| 분류@ | peda activity정보를가지고있는한사람이다른사람에게 AHS 전달해 주거나, 정보의형태를바꾸는활동. 단순한정보전달로상호작용이제한되어 있다.Information-gap activity, which involves a transfer of given informationfrom one person to another—or from one form to another, or from oneplace to another. One example is pair work in which each member of thepair has a part of the total information (for example an incomplete picture)and attempts to convey it verbally to the other.@ Opinion-gap activity주어진상황에대해개인적인기호나 느낌, 태도 SS 밝히는 활동. 주로토론이나논쟁에서쓰이며, 학습자가어느정도의복잡한언어형태를사용할수있어야하므로 EFL 상황에서는한계가 있다.Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers ig) AeOpinion-gap activity, which involves identifying and articulating a personalpreference, feeling, or attitude in response to a given situation. One exampleis story completion; another is taking part in the discussion of a socialissue. The activity may involve using factual information and formulatingarguments to justify one’s opinion, but there is no objective procedure fordemonstrating outcomes as right or wrong, and no reason to expect thesame outcome from different individuals or on different occasions.@ Reasoning-gap activity주어진정보를토대로 추론, AAA 방법, 관련성이나형태에대한인식 SS 통해새로운정보를도출하는 활동. 하나의결과물을위해긴밀한상호작용과그룹구성원과의활발한정보교류를촉진하기때문에효과적 이다.Reasoning-gap activity, which involves driving some new informationfrom given information through processes of inference, deduction, practicalreasoning, or a perception of relationships or patterns. One example isdeciding what course of action is best (for example cheapest or quickest)for a given purpose and within given constraint. The activity necessarilyinvolves comprehending and conveying information, as an information-gapactivity, but the information to be conveyed is not identical with the initiallycomprehended.There is a piece of reasoning which connects the two.2, Richards2| 분류@ Jigsaw tasks : 각각다른정보의 2 내 fe 합쳐전체를만드는활동Ex, 전체의이야기를세 PROS 나누고, 3 명의학습자가서로다른부분을맡아하나의이야기로만드는활동@ Information-gap tasks : 한명의학생이일부정보를갖고다른학생이상보적인정보를 Zt고서로상호작용을통해상대방의는(3) Problem-solving tasks : 학생들책에도달ᄒ | 는활활동. 일반적으로o으로 SL [의@ Decision-making tasks : 학생들이주어진문제에대한여러가지대안중협상과토론을통하여한가지를선택하는활동© Opinion exchange tasks : 학생들이토론에참여하여각자의생각을교환하는 활동. 하나으결론에도달해야할필요는 없다.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 117118Practical English Language Teaching3. For beginning students@ A guided conversation (also called controlled conversation)It is an old technique from the audiolingual era that is still useful for lower-level students. Error Treatment유창성을넘어서정확성에도 BAS | 교사는학생이생성한 OF 중어느오류에대해서, 언제, 어떤방식으로피드백을제공할것인지결정하고효과적인 EMS서제공해야 한다.(1) To what and when? - 어떤오류를언제수정할 것인가?교사는학습자들의참여를유도하기위해서학생의오류를하나의학습과정으로인식 하고, 오류수정은학습목표에따라진행해야 한다. 즉 , 교실수업의목표가정확성에있는경우즉각적으로피드백을제공하지만의사소통에초점을둘경우RU HOT 4 0의사소통활동이끝난후에피드백을제공하는것이바람직하다Chapter 02 Productive Skills 171PartPractical English Language TeachingHypercorrection can create a negative classroom atmosphere, discouraginglearners from risk-taking and experimentation. The extent of error correctionwill depend on the aim of the lesson.* When the focus is on meaning, it is inappropriate to interrupt the flow ofinteraction. In these situations, the teacher can make a note of errors forfollow-up treatment later.* When the focus is on form, the teacher might well interrupt before thestudents have finished their turn.Teachers provide positive feedback in acknowledging a learner’sutterance for many reasons.ᆞ To confirm a learner’s utterance regarding features such as gram-matical correctness, word choice, or any particular content* To praise learners for their performanceᆞ To encourage them for their attempts in using languageA teacher's negative or corrective feedback can be categorized asdirect (explicit) or indirect (implicit) strategies.ᆞ Indirect strategies implicitly provide a correct model of the errorwithout telling them overtly what the mistake was.* Explicit strategies point directly to a learner’s error.@® Indirect / Implicit feedback북시적으로교사가오류를수정하거나오류가 VSS 암시하는전략으로정확성보다는의미에보다초점이있는경우사용한 다. 묵시자가 2=Al(self—correction)-& 유도할수있지만학습자가오류를알아차리지못할수도 있다.(8) RecastA teacher reformulates all parts of a student’s utterance minus the error.Ex, T: What did you do yesterday?S: 1 go shopping.T: Oh, you went shopping. Where did you go?122 Build-up 영어교육론(6) Clarification requestA teacher uses phrases such as “Pardon me?” or “I don’t understand.”,or asks another questions such as “What do you mean by that?”. Thisrequest signals to the students that there was some kind of error, orsomething was not clear in their language use, and invites them toreformulate their utterance. Teachers use this feedback when studentsmake meaning related errors while the focus is on communication.Ex, T: How old are you?S: Thirty.T: Pardon me?S: Thirteen.(2) Direct 7 Explicit feedback명시적으로학습자의오류를지적해주는전략 으로, 교사가정확한답을제공하거나혹은오류가있는부분을지적함 6으로써학습자가자신의오류에대해주목을하게된다. 보다효과적인언어 SSS 위해서는교사가정답을제공하기보다는학습자스스로수정하도록유도하는것이바람직하 다.(a) Correct answer feedbackThe teacher directly tells a student what mistake was and provides thecorrect answer. For example, she might say, “oh, you mean...,” or “youshould say...,” or “the correct form of this verb form is...” An alternativeof this strategy is to ask a peer student, other than the one whocommitted the error, to provide the correct answer.T: Where did you go after class yesterday?S: I go home.T: Go is not the correct past tense form. You need to say, “I wenthome.”(6) Guided feedbackA more effective strategy than direct correction is to provide the studentsan opportunity to self-repair and guide them toward the correct answer.Strategies that allow the teacher to do so are normally referred to aselicitation techniques. The purpose of such strategies is to help the studentsnotice that something was wrong, locate the mistake(s), and/or providemetalinguistic feedback, that is, some information about the mistake.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 12 3Guideline for Pre-service Teachers a ᅵPart124Practical English Language Teaching* Metalinguistic feedback— It contains either comments, informations regarding the accuracy of astudent’s utterance without providing the correct form.T.: Where did you go after class yesterday?S: Igo home.T : How do you say this in simple past tense?- The teacher can also provide general reminders simply by referringto a particular lesson or class. In doing so, the teacher activatesgrammatical rules the student has dealt with before.T.: Where did you go after class yesterday?S : I go home.T : Do you remember the grammar we focused on in class yesterday?(©) Teacher’s request to repeat (with corrective intent)The teacher asks the student to repeat with an error corrective intent inmind. This response may indicate that the teacher did not understandwhat the students had said, or that the students’ utterances contained amistake. While the intention of this strategy is to let the students knowthat there was an error in their response, it does not point out whatwas wrong.T : Where did you go after class yesterday?S : I go home.T.: Where did you go? Can you say this again? Your answer wasnot grammatically correct.@ Asking questionsThe teacher asks a particular question about the mistake. For example,“How do we say this in English?” By asking specific questions, mostteachers indirectly provide some information about what a student’sactual mistake was. This strategy is also a form of metalinguisticfeedback.Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers | 휴T : Where are you going later?S : lam going later shopping on.T : What should be the correct word order in your sentence?©) PinpointingThere are different ways of pointing out which part of a student’sutterance is wrong and in need of repair. One strategy is to echo thefaulty utterance. The teacher repeats the students’ ill-formed utterancewithout correction, but pronounces the feature with exaggeration.S : On the table there’s a red cup.T : Um, hmm, but you said “a Red Cup” (Emphasizing) What else?() PausingAnother strategy involves pausing. The instructor repeats the learner’sutterance up to the point of the error, where the student needs to self-correct.T : Where are you going later?5 : lam go to the supermarket?T : Iam...9 : 1am going to the supermarket.9. I played baseball with my friends,Did you drive here?(Practical English Language Teaching Speaking)Build-up 영어교육론 IIGuideline for Pre-service Teachers 3)Comments : |It is often the case that pronunciation issues interacts with grammar issues. As aresult, if learners mispronounce key sounds, it can seem like they are producingungrammatical utterances.One very important grammar point that beginning learnersoften work on is the past tense and other cases were verbs end in —ed. Depending onthe surrounding sounds, the —ed ending can be pronounced in three different ways.Also, particularly for beginning learners in EFL situations, and especially for thosewho have had mostly reading exposure to English (not much listening exposure),there is sometimes a tendency to pronounce the ~ed as if it were a syllable no matterwhere it occurs. For instance, students may correctly say “hunted” as two syllables,but then also say “roped” as “ro-ped” or “pulled” as “pulled” because the spellingsuggests that --ed is a syllable to be said. For learners whose native language doesn’tuse Consonant clusters at the end of words, pronouncing the English past tense andother —ed endings can be very difficult. It will take some practice on learners’ partand some explanation on yours.(2) Too—down approach : focus on suprasegmentals (intonation, rhythm, stress)억양, 강세및리듬의초분절적인요소는의미에직접적인 SYS 끼치므로적절한지도가이루어지지않을경우의사소통에장애가될뿐아니라때로는무례한듯한인상을남길수 있다.Suprasegmentals include intonation, rhythm, and stress. These featurescan have an even greater impact on intelligibility than the mispronunciationof sounds. Thus, the focus has shifted to fluency rather than accuracyencouraging an emphasis on suprasementals.a Now, you need to add 0010 cream.| Now, you need to add cold créam.T lost my red scarf. Controlled PracticeOnce your learners begin to perceive patterns, your instruction can turnto activities that provide opportunity to say the target sounds repeatedly,but in a meaningful context.Picture storiesCollect pictures of places and items that begin with a target sound.Tell the class the story and then have them recall the order and tellthe story. Then have them shuffle the cards and change the story.Students may also find pictures of items in a magazine that use thesound and make up a new story to tell a partner.2. Guided Practice / Communicative PracticeFinally, it is important that learners practice pronunciation patternsin unplanned, extended speech (much like ‘authentic use’ activities)mentioned. The activities will not be completely spontaneous becauseteachers guide the students to use particular pronunciation patterns.Information gap activities_ Unreadable fax: Each student has a copy of a work document that ismissing key figures (including teens/tens combinations). Pairs workitogether to complete their copy of the document.132 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 8B E(02) Teaching Writing 01. Product vs. Process—oriented Approach(1) Product-oriented approach글쓰기 Se (writing) °| ae BOA 과정보다는그 AvHE (product, outcome)초점을 두고, 오류가없는완벽한쓰기활동을진행하게 된다.@ Product-oriented approaches focus on the final product, the coherent,error-free text.@) This approach focuses on tasks in which the learner imitates, copies, andtransforms models provided by the teacher and/or the textbook.(03) The focus is on the sentence level grammar and discourse that is built upby fitting sentences together.@ It is consistent with sentence-level structuralist linguistics and bottom-upprocessing.© It focuses on getting it right and the final product is evaluated.© It usually accompanies with controlled task following models.@ly In the ClassroomProduct-oriented approach2012 학년도기출Teaching procedure:1. The teacher shows pictures of pets to students and asks what kinds ofpets they like.2. The teacher gives each of the students a short story of a dog and a setof four sequential pictures showing its storyline, telling them that theyare going to read and write the story as accurately as possible. The storycontains a number of regular past tense verbs.3. Students read the story silently for 3 minutes and return the story to theteacher but keep the pictures.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 1334. After putting some key words from the story on the board, the teacherreads the whole story aloud.5. With the aid of the pictures and key words, students write the story asclosely as they can remember.6. The teacher collects students’ writings and later corrects them by crossingout incorrect regular past tense forms, providing corresponding correctforms above them.7.In the next class, students receive their writings and look over theirerrors and the teacher’s corrections.(2) Process—oriented approach134글쓰기 SES 하나의사고과정이라생각하고작가의생각을글로옮기는과정을중시하는접근법 이다. 따라서무엇을쓰느냐가아니라어떻게쓰느냐에초점을맞추고글을수정하는과정자체를중시 한다.(@) Process-oriented approaches focus on the steps involved in drafting andredrafting a piece of work.00) There will never be the perfect text, but one can get closer to perfectionthrough producing, reflection on, discussing and reworking successivedrafts of a text.© Teachers focus less on a perfect final product than on the development ofsuccessive drafts of a text.@ The focus is on quantity rather than quality. Thus, writers are encouragedto get their ideas onto paper without worrying too much about formalcorrectness in the initial stages.(6) Students share their work with others, getting feedback on their ideas andhow they are expressed.© Higher order choices (for example, discourse context). determine lowerorder ones such as how to package information within a sentence, andwhat grammatical forms to use.Build-up 영어교육론 11—ly In the Classroom00008Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) JaneProcess-oriented approach2009 학년도기출Teaching procedure:1. The teacher sets up guidelines on how to write essays.2. The teacher explains to the students how to use multimedia during thewriting process.3. The teacher collects the first drafts of the students’ essays via e-mail.4. The teacher opens up an online blog for the class to post the first draftsof their essays.5. Each student reads one of his/her peers’ essays and posts three well-thought-out feedback statements on the blog.6. The teacher asks the students to read the feedback received from theirpeers and to revise their first drafts. When they have questions about thefeedback, they should e-mail them to their feedback providers.7. The teacher gives his/her own feedback to each student via e-mail.8. The teacher asks the students to post their revised essays on the blog.2. Writing Stages Based on Process—oriented Approach(1) Pre—writing stage0Orof&bs건loAnoaux적신힘~랄동(8) Brainstorming*It is often a group exercise in which all students in the class areencouraged to participate by sharing their collective knowledgeabout a particular subject.« A teacher suggests a broad topic.¢ Students call out as many associations as possible.ᆞ The teacher can then write on the board.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 135Practical English Language Teaching(b) Freewriting (Quickwriting)ᆞ The main idea of this techniques is for students to write for a specificperiod time (usually 5-10 minutes) without stopping.ᆞ Free from the necessity of worrying about grammar and format.* A teacher provides an opening clause or sentence for the students tostart with.- After copying this sentence, students write down whatever comesinto their heads.ᆞ The freewriting generated can be raw material to use in addressingthe writing assignment at hand.©) Clustering (Wordmapping)* Clustering begins a key word or central idea placed in the center of apage around which the student jots down in a few minutes all of thefree associations triggered by the subject matter.ᆞ The words or phrases generated are put on the page or board in apattern which takes shapes from the connections the writer sees aseach new thought emerges.ᆞ Writers can be exposed to a wide variety of approaches to the topicwhich might further generate material for writing.* It can get in tough with the right-hemisphere part of the brain.(2) While— and Post writing stage@ SY: 본격적인작문과점검활동이 일어난다. 점검활동은먼저내용의적합성(appropriateness)o]]4] 시작하여글의정확성 (60047807/ 으로초점이이동 한다.(0) 활동(@) Peer-editing (after first draft)Students step out of their own selves, to see what they have createdthrough the eyes of others to discover the impact of their words on thethoughts of their readers, so that they can then uses the information toimprove what we have written. We call this peer-editing. Through careful questioning, the teacher can supporta student writer in getting ideas together, organizing them, and findingappropriate language.Pus |Steps of the Writing Process1. PrewriteIn this important first step, students are given an opportunity to prepare towrite and to collect their thoughts and ideas. If done properly, it can easestudents into writing without any hesitation or worry.2. WriteLearners write down all of their ideas. They do not worry about form orcorrectness or even the order. The objective is to get the ideas on paper asquickly and flow together.3. ReviseThe initial piece of writing is examined and reworked so that the ideas arelogical and flow together.4. EditLearners (with the help of their teachers or classmates) proof-read their workto make sure that there are not any content errors or grammatical or spellingerrors.5. PublishThe writing piece is rewritten in a published or presentable form, in a student-made book, on special paper, and/or on a computer so that it can be displayedor shared.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 137138PartPractical English Language Teaching@ly In the ClassroomSample Writing Lesson1. Read the whole piece through first before you writeanything.* Look for strengths as well as weaknesses, and let the student knowwhat the strengths are.*If you use any editing symbols, make sure that the students arefamiliar with all of them and know what to do when they see one.Provide opportunities for the students to use the symbols, too.Chapter 02 Productive Skills 139PartPractical English Language Teaching* Work out your own strategy for handling errors and explain it to yourstudents. Decide if you will correct or simply indicate where theyoccur, if you will deal only with the errors you have discussed in class,with errors of a certain type, or with all errors; decide what importanceyou attach to grammatical errors and, again, let your students know.ᆞ Remember that when you or any other reader responds to a student’spiece of writing, your main job is not to pass judgement on its quality,but to help the writer see what to do next. Ask students to listen to a five-minute lecture while jotting down themain points. Then, give students four minutes to summarize the lectureusing their notes.2. Ask students to listen to the lecture again while they write down as manyadditional main points of the lecture as possible. Read the passage below and follow the directions.Purpose: To provide students with an opportunity to share privately inwriting their reaction, questions, and concerns about school experienceswith the teacher without any threat of reprisal or evaluation.Rationale: The notion of these strategies is a partial refinement ofjournal writing. Their major characteristic is the importance given tocommunications between the student and the teacher. They provide theteacher with the opportunity not only to learn what students are thinkingand doing but also to share thoughts and suggestions with them.Often journals were used to encourage diarylike entries of what tookplace in the way of progress on a project; sometimes they were usedto give students the opportunity to respond freely to what took place atschool or home, or to respond to a book or some other forms of literature.While the teacher might not respond to every entry, the intent of thisactivity is to have students write to the teacher and to have the teacherwrite a genuine response to the student. The teacher does not evaluate thestudent’s comments as either right or wrong. What is important to note isthe teacher’s respect for the privacy of journal as well as the nonjudgmentaland nonprescriptive nature of the teacher’s reaction. Discussions to bemade are left up to the student.Intended Audience: can be used with students of 9th grade and over inKorea.Write the name of this teaching technique in TWO words.| Your answer |Chapter 02 Productive Skills 159Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) ᅵPractical English Language Teaching02. Decide the part of speech of the unknown word.B. Look for further clues in the word’s immediate collocates.C. Look at the wider context, including the surrounding clauses andsentences.D. Look at the form of the word for any clues as to meaning.E. Make a guess as to the meaning of the word, on the above strategies.F. Read on and see if the guess is confirmed; if not-and if the word seemscritical to the understanding of the text, go back and repeat the abovesteps. If the word does not seem critical, carry on reading. Maybe themeaning will become clearer later on.다양한 UA S(Ex, 접두사, 접미사, 동의어, 반의어등 ) 을활용하여문맥속에서해당어휘의의미를주론하는 ASS 개발하도록장려해야 한다.Chapter 03 Vocabulary 200 Grammar 16 7PartPractical English Language Teaching© 계획되지 PEE’ 어휘지도를실시 하라.Engage in ‘unplanned’ vocabulary teaching.부분의경우어휘지도는즉흥적으로실시 된다. 즉 , 학생이특정어휘의의미를물어 보거나, 학습활동속에서등장한특정어휘를다룰필요가있다고판단되는 경우,어휘지도가실시되는 것이다. 이러한즉홍적인어휘지도는매우중요 하다. 때때로SSA 어휘지도를확장시켜여러가지예를제시하거나다른문장속에서해당어휘를사용하도록장려할수도 있다. 단 , 즉흥적어휘지도에너무많은시간을할애하여본시학습활동에 SES 주어서는안될 것이다.2. Techniques(1) Keyword methodKeyword method 목표어와비슷한철자나발음을가진모국어와연결시키거나이미지와단어를연결시켜 Hols 암기하는방법 이다.»—~oOKeyword method is called a mnemonic device, which helps to link a wordform and its meaning and to consolidate this linkage in memory. There arethree stages.@ The learner choose L1 and L2 word, preferable a concrete entity, based ona phonological or orthographic similarity with the target word.(2) Strong association between the target word and the keyword must beconstructed so that, when seeing or hearing the target word, the learner isreminded immediately of the keyword.(3) A visual image is constructed to combine the referents of the keyword andthe target word, preferably an odd or bizarre image that will help make itmore memorable.(2) Word mapWord maps are an extremely engaging way of building up vocabulary knowledgeas well as provoking students into retrieving and using what they know.(+) The word map takes shapebathroome + oesitting room bedroomCutilty ron hee ~ study )( 0006 ) kitchen toilet)frying pan(Jeremy Harmer, The Practice of English Language Teaching)174 Build-up 영어교육론ᄆGuideline for Pre-service Teachers 33)| Example |2011 학년도기출Activity Procedure(1) Work in groups of three and choose one topic from the list below:computer, country, family, food, hobbyholiday, library, movie, school, sport(2) Brainstorm with your group members, and make a word web like theexample shown below for the topic of your choice. For the boxes,come up with words (i.e., subtopics) that are related to the topic.(3) Choose two subtopics and write, in the ovals, words that are related tothem.(4) Make sure to leave the pentagon and two boxes blank so that the topicand subtopics may be guessed by other groups.(5) Show your web to other groups, and ask them to guess the topic andsubtopics that should be in the pentagon and boxes, respectively, ofyour web.Example| textbook |teacher |principal ||| % /I\\math history nervous studybiology - prepare difficultChapter 03 Vocabulary and Grammar 175PartPractical English Language Teaching© a. Approach to FFT (Form—focused Instruction)(1) Focus on meaning언어의의미와 nee 통에초점을 = ADA(meaning based approach)°2교실수업내에서문법교육은중시되지 않는다.(2) Focus on forms과거에문법지도가진행되었던방식 으로, 정확성에만 RAS 두어문법지도를실시한 다.의자소통상황과문법지도를연계시키지않고탈맥락화 (4600116※1[14811281102) 된문법학습이 일어난다,(3) Focus on form현재의사소통접근법에가장부합되는문법지도접근법으로의미에제 1 의 #24 (meaning1{78\) 을두고그다음으로정확성에 2.4ilform second)& 두게 된다. 하지만언어의의미와정확성 Dol] 초점을둔다는점에서 focus on meaning#} focus on forms approach2]법지도와는큰차이가 있다.Focus on form refers to the practice of explicitly drawing students’ attentionto linguistic features within the context meaning-focused activities. In otherwords, communication comes first, and a focus on form comes second. Theadvantage of this reorientation is that “learner’s attention is drawn preciselyto a linguistic feature as necessitated by a communicative demand.” Learnersare therefore more likely to see the relationship between language form andcommunicative function.«Implication : Teachers should present the grammar in a context that makesclear the relationship between the grammatical form and the communicativefunction.178 Build-up 영어교육론07)ly In the Classroom|L Get Readyis4g2:Guideline for Pre-service Teachers &Look.at the people and readthe words. Deductive vs. Inductive Approach법지도에서연역적인접근법age] 학슴스타일이나교실관계 이다.상호so] 따라적절히혼용되어야하는배타적인관계가아니라장호보완적인The deductive and inductive approaches are not mutually exclusive, andmost teachers need to deploy both in their teaching.(1) Deductive approach(A4H4e! 접근법)먼저규칙을제시한후이규칙을주어진예들에적용하도록 한다.The teacher presents the grammar rule and then gives students exercises inwhich they apply the rule.(8) rule-driven learning09 traditional Grammar-Translation approach+ It gets straight ¢ to the point and cantherefore be time-saving. Many rulescan be more quickly explained thanelicited, thereby allowing more time forpractice and application.« It respects the intelligence and maturityof many students and acknowledgesthe role of cognitive processes in lan-guage acquisition.* It confirms many students’ expectationsabout classroom learning, particularlyfor those with an analytical learningstyle.* It allows for teachers to deal with lan-guage points as they come up, ratherthan having to anticipate them and pre-pare for them in advance.. Staring the lesson with a grammar ex-planation may be frustrating for somestudents, especially younger ones. Theymay not have sufficient metalanguageor may not be able to understand theconcepts involved.ᆞ Grammar explanation encourages a tea-cher-fronted, transmission style class-room.ᆞ Explanation is seldom as memorableas other forms of presentation, such asdemonstration.* Such an approach encourages the be-lief that learning a language is simply acase of knowing the rules.181Chapter 03 Vocabulary and GrammarGuideline for Pre-service Teachers G3) =PartPractical English Language Teaching| Example |Nouns, adjectivesand adverbs1Subject and object pronounsSubject pronouns| I you | he | she | it | we | you they |Object pronouns| me | you | him | her | it | us | you | them |@ The subject is the person or thing doing the action:I left early.She went home.We said goodbye.e The object is the person or thing receiving the action :She telephoned me.| hit him.We saw her.Write the correct pronouns for these sentences:lett early.1 telephoned yesterday. memorable and serviceable.*The mental effort. involved. ensuresgreater cognitive depth, again ensuringgreater memorability.¢ Students are more actively involved inthe learning process and are thereforelikely to be more attentive and moti-vated.*It favors patter-recognition and prob-lem-solving and is therefore particularlysuited to learners who like this kind ofchallenge.- If the energy spent working outrules may mislead students into believ-ing that rules are the objective of lan-guage learning.ᆞ The time spent in working out a rulemay be at the expense of time spentputting the rule into productive prac-tice.« Students may hypothesize the wrongrule, or their version of the rule may beeither too broad or too narrow.«It can place heavy demands on teach-ers in planning a
