Explicit vs. Implicit Grammar Instructiond(explicit)@] 문법지도에서는규칙이직접적으로제시되기때문에학생들은을한눈에알수 있다. 그러나 BAA(implicit)el 문법지도에서는규칙이으로제시되지않고주어진언어적자료에암시되어 있다.명시규칙칙직접oDPe aIn explicit grammar instruction, grammar rules are clearly defined andexplicitly stated. The rules are fully and clearly expressed and readilyobservable. On the other hand, implicit grammar instruction rejects theneed for any kind or explicit focus on form. This is based on the beliefthat learners can acquire language naturally if they receive sufficientcomprehensible input from the teacher. In implicit grammar instruction, therules are implied or understood though not directly addressed and containedin the nature though not readily apparent.Chapter 03 Vocabulary and Grammar 18/7Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 33 ~Practical English Language Teaching2012 학년도기출Teaching ProcedureStep 1: The teacher asks students where they went last summer and whatthey took on their journey. Then she writes down the following sentenceson the board and explains the difference in form and meaning between thetwo sentences using the terms ‘past tense’ and ‘past participle (pp)’.I took a light jacket.1 should have taken a warm jacket.Step 2: The teacher hands out a story from a magazine that includes the targetstructure ‘should+have+pp’. She asks students to read the story carefully andlook for the examples of ‘shouldt+thave+pp’ in the given text.Kate travelled across the Australian desert. She made nopreparations. She didn’t take a map, and she didn’t take a cellphone. Soon after she set off, she got lost and got trapped in aflash flood. Later, looking back on it, she said, “I should havetaken a map. I should have taken a cell phone...”~ ... ~” 가세”Step 3: The teacher asks students to think about their own previousjourney and complete the worksheet below.WorksheetI on my I should havejourney. on my journey.I took a light jacket on my _| I should have taken a warmjacket on my journey. journey.188 Build-up 영어교육론Step 4: The teacher asks students to write a story using the sentences theyhave produced in the worksheet above, and to share their writingswith the partners.4. Declarative vs. Procedural KnowledgeAWA Z\Al(Declarative knowledge) 언어규칙에대해서알고규칙을 Aged 수있는지식을말하는데비해절차적지식 ( ᄆ 700604781 knowledge)2 의사소통을위해규칙을사용하는능력을 말한다.Declarative knowledge is knowing language rules. Procedural knowledgeis being able to use the knowledge for communication. Those who havedeclarative knowledge can state or explain the rule, but those who do nothave procedural knowledge can not use the rule when using the language tocommunicate.* For example, the students who can tell that they have to put an -s on theend of the verb when making third person singular declarative statementshave declarative knowledge, but not procedural knowledge.* While declarative knowledge can facilitate the development of proceduralknowledge, it is not a necessary and sufficient condition for the developmentof such knowledge.Chapter 03 Vocabulary and Grammar 189Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) ※PartPractical English Language Teaching2011 학년도기출Activity AChange the sentences as in the example, and check your answers withyour partner. Learners are not required to use or practice the target item.(2) Input processing교사는학습자들에게목표구문의형태보다목표구문과관련있는그림등을먼저제시 한다. 학생들은형태보다의미를먼저접한뒤형태와의미를 결합, 연관지음으로써구문을학습하게 된다.@ Learners need structured input activities that enable them focus onmeaning while attending to form before they are expected to use thelanguage to produce output.@) The goal of input processing instruction is encourage learners to makebetter form-meaning connections than they would be if left to their owndevices.(3) Guideline for input processing activities(8) Present one thing at a time(6) Move from sentences to connected discourse© Keep meaning in focus@ Use both oral and written input©) Have the learner ‘do something’ with the inputBuild-up 영어교육론 11Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 33)Choose the sentence that goes with the picture.(a) The man bit a snake. | @ The elephant frightened|@® The mother fed the child.(6) The man was bitten by| _ the mouse. 06) The mother was fed bya snake. (©) The elephant was fright-, — the child.ened by the mouse.* Students are encouraged to match picture with italic-typed formswhich carry the active and passive voice. In other words, a form-meaning relationship in the picture explains the use of the passive totopicalize the patient of a sentence by placing it in subject position.* The picture leads learners to attend to the form of the verb todetermine whether the subject is the agent of the verb, as is mostgenerally the case with active verb, or the patient, as is the case withpassive verbs.ᆞ The worksheet represents a structured-input activity where learnershave the chance to process the target feature in a controlled manner.Unlike the traditional grammar instruction, this activity is designedto help learners naturally process input in accordance with theirinterlanguage.Chapter 03 Vocabulary and Grammar 193PartPractical English Language Teaching(3) Consciousness—raising tasks학슴자들에게해당규칙이적용된일련의예들을제공한뒤규칙을도출하도록하고그 FAG 자신의상황에맞게 적용, ease 단게로 이루어진다.CR tasks consist of data containing exemplars of the targeted feature andinstructions requiring the learners to operate on the data in some way.@ Main characteristics of CR tasksᆞ There is an attempt to isolate a specific linguistic feature for focusedattention.ᆞ The learners are provided with data that illustrate the targeted featureand they may also be provided with an explicit rule describing orexplaining the feature.ᆞ The learners are expected to utilize intellectual effort to understand thetargeted feature.* Learners may be optionally required to verbalize a rule describing thegrammatical structure.@) Differences between Input processing and CR taskInput processing? 언어의형태가아닌의미에초점을 FE 묵시적기초하는데비해 OR task: 언어형태에초점을두고규칙을생성하도록하는명시적인접근법을취한 다.* Whereas input processing tasks are implicit learning, CR tasks are designedto cater primarily to explicit learning. Thus, the desired outcome of a CRtask is awareness of how some linguistic feature works.* While Input processing tasks are built around content of a generalnature, for example, stories, pictures of objects, opinions, CR tasks makelanguage itself the content.194 Build-up 영어교육론끄Guideline for Pre-service TeachersA What is the difference between verbs like ‘give’ and ‘explain?’She gave a book to her father. A teacher might collect a set of student assignmentsand use a concordancing program to analyse examples of learners’ languagelooking for typical error patterns. Systematic errors in learners’ writing canbe used as a basis for the development of learning materials. Alternatively, ateacher might look through established corpora of texts by native speakersof the target language and find examples for patterns and present these tolearners as examples of adapt them into exercises. Learners themselves canbe trained in the use of a concordancing program and corpora, then becometheir own researchers finding examples and developing their own rules forgrammatical structures, idioms and general usage, for example, investigatingthe differences between look and see. This approach is often called DataDriven Learning.204 Build-up 영어교육론Data Driven Learning학습자들이언어패턴과규칙을콘코던스 aan 통해익히는귀납적접근방법 이다.학습자들은패턴과규칙스럽게 ` 내재화 "시킨다. 이접근방법은학습자들의언어에대한흥미를자극하고스스로언어교육에대한책임을갖도록해준다.주도 ofof |NHLau)clrData Driven Learning (DDL) is an inductive approach to learning in whichlearners acquire an understanding of language patterns and rules bybecoming more involved researching corpora, usually through the use ofa computer-based concordancing program. Instead of studying patternsand rules, learners naturally internalize them. This approach can stimulatelearners’ interest in language and give them a sense of empowerment andresponsibility for their own language education.컴퓨터를활용한의사소통은컴퓨터매개의사소통 (2140) 이라고 불리며, CALL}we 가장잘알려진활동들중의 하나이다. 0140 는 이메일, 게시판, 채팅과 MOOS연다포함 하는데, 이것자체가언어학습을반드시동반하는것은 아니지만, 목표어로의미협상을할때언어학습이일어나게 된다. 영어교사들은서로다른나라의들이 CMCS 통해목표어로의사소통을하는과제를줄수 있다.Communicating using the computer is often referred to as computer-medicatedcommunication (CMC) and is one of the more popular activities associated withCALL. CMC encompasses communication by email, bulletin boards, chatlinesand within MOO (Multi-user domains, Object-oriented) environments. CMCrefers to a situation in which computer-based discussion may take place butwithout necessarily involving learning. Of course, opportunities for learning areinherently present, especially in situations in which learners need to engagein negotiation of meaning with native speakers of the target language or evenwith peers of non-native proficiency. It is common for teachers in differentChapter 04 Computer—assisted Language Learning 205Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) ,countries to create assignments for their students to communicate in a commontarget language, for example, students in Korea and Brazil both learning Englishworking together to collect information about each other’s interests and studies.(1) Asynchronous mode학습자들이동시에인터넷에접속할필요없이컴퓨터를매개체로하여 이루어진다.따라서학생들간의의사소통에는시간차 (1026 gap)7} 존재한 다. 6-1914 이나 bulletinboard 둥이이에해당 한다.Ex, keypal projecte-mail 활용한 _Keypal project 특히다른문화권의같은 또래, 비슷한수준의학생들과메일을주고받는다는점에서문화를초월한의사소통을가능하게 한다.Keypals is the term for pen pals who use email to communicate and providesa simple and effective way of putting learners in touch with other learners inother parts of the world. Learners can talk about their experiences of learningEnglish, and email is the perfect medium for cross-cultural communication.Learning English, other countries and culturesTo find out about another country and what it’s like learning EnglishthereYoung learners and adult learners, elementary level and higher5 lessons of 1 hour each* Contact a teacher in another country and exchange detailed informa-tion about your classes* Decide exactly how you will pair up your learners with the otherteachers’ learners, and whether pairs will be using their own emailaccount.206 Build-up 영어교육론. Pairwork using the Internet. Tell your learners that they will be contact-ing leaners in another country. First, they will need to find out somebasic information about that country.. Brainstorm what learners already know about the country and giveeach group a topic to research. Give them a time limit to find out asmuch. as they can.. Writing an introductory email. Tell your learners the name of the key-pal they will be sending their email to. Learners compose an email tothis keypal including information about themselves and their country,and the questions.. Checking and revising the email. Learners now exchange their draftemail with classmates for checking. As the email will be sent to anothercountry and to someone they don’t know, learners are usually verykeen for their email to be as ‘correct’as possible.5. Learners correct their email and send the email to their keypal.. Learners receive and read their emails.. Learners write a short reply thanking their keypal, and answering thequestions in the email. Again, learners check and revise their emailsbefore sending.. Learners receive and read their second emails to prepare a poster or pre-sentation describing what they have learnt about the other country.. Learners in their small groups present their findings to the class. At theend of all the presentations, you could have the class vote ‘prizes’ forwhose presentation was the most.Information on what learners have found out about the other country canbe presented using other ICT tools such as a blog or a wiki. A culturalbox of real objects can be posted to the partner class.(2) Synchronous학습자들이컴퓨터와인터넷을매개로의사소통을하기위해서동시간대에인터넷BS 해야 한다. 즉각적인상호작용과피드백이이루어진다는장점이있지만시간과공간의제약을받는다는단점도 있다.Ex, Chat programs, Video conferencingChapter 04 Computer—assisted Language Learning _ 207iiGuideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) .MOO stands for ‘multi-user object-oriented dimension’. It is a permanentspace on the Internet set aside for a specific group, a virtual environment.You could call it an online community.|? Example |Getting learners involved in conferencing on a MOOThe first step in getting learners involved in learning on a MOO is to getthem involved in a conferencing, which allows both teacher and studentto keep files of what has been said. The procedure is as follows:1. Introduce the students to the basics of MOOing. Take the class to aMOO in small groups and have them communicate with each other sothey get used to the unique environment.2. Collect the first drafts of an essay from the students (via email). Havea copy of the draft with you for reference during the conference(either printed out or on-screen in a separate window).3. Set up conferences for each student. Ask the students to bring threequestions regarding their essay to the conference.4. Meet each student at the MOO to discuss the draft, focusing onquestions they bring.5. Through non-verbal gestures, encourage the student to do most of the ‘talking.’6. Lead the students to state clearly by the end of the conference whatthey will focus on during the revision process.208 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 33) |7. Have the students save a log of the conversation to their hard drive ora floppy disk, or do it your self and send it to the student in an emailmessage.c> The advantages of such environments to learning a language is that alearner can enter into an environment where a target language is beingspoken and be forced to react to others’ words and actions.(4) e-learning인터넷, CD-ROM, MP38Uy 휴대폰과같은휴대용기기를이용하여학습하는 AS가리킨다.It refers to learning that takes place using technology such as the Internet,CD-ROMs and portable devices like mobile phones or MP3 players.There are several terms associated with e-learning, which are often usedinterchangeably and which can be rather confusing.@® Distance learningThe term distance learning originally applied to traditional paper-baseddistance courses delivered by mail. Nowadays distance learning includeslearning via technology such as the Internet, CD-ROMs and mobiletechnologies, hence the newer term e-learning. Distance or e-learning areoften used as umbrella names for the terms below.(2) Open learningThis is one aspect of distance learning and simply refers to how muchindependence the learner has. The more open a distance course is, themore autonomy the learner has in deciding what course content to cover,how to do so and when.(8) Online learningThis is learning which takes place via the Internet. As such, onlinelearning is a facet of e-learning.Chapter 04 Computer—assisted Language Learning 209Practical English Language Teaching@ Blended learningThis is a mixture of online and face-to-face course delivery. Forexample, learners might meet once a week with a teacher face-to-facefor an hour, and do a further two hours’ work weekly online. In somesituations the digital element is done offline with a CD-ROM.(5) Computer—adaptive testing (CAT)CATS 각시험의난이도를학습자의능력에맞추어주는평가 이다. 학습자들은컴퓨터를통해 NGS 치며, 컴퓨터가즉각적으로각문항을채점하면서그다음문항은학습자의단계에따라다르게 주어진다. 주어진문제를맞히면그다음문제는더어려운것이 나오며, 주어진문제를틀리면다음문제는더쉬운것이 나온다.CATS] 큰장점은대규모교실에서도학습자들은각자자신의능력에따라맞춤화된다른시험을보게된다는 것이다. 그러나 CATS 개발하는것이쉽지않다는 것과,학습자들은이미한번응답한것에대해서는다시볼수도없고답을없다는한계가 있다.Computer-adaptive testing (CAT) uses a database of questions to matchthe difficulty of each test item to the abilities of the learners being tested.Learners take a CAT test at the computer and because the computer caninstantly mark each answer, the following question can be tailored oradapted. If a learner correctly answer a question, the computer will ensurethat the next question will be more difficult. If a learner incorrectly answers aquestion, the next question will be easier.One of the great advantages of CAT testing is that randomization of testitems can ensure that learners of a large class taking a test in the same roommay all take slightly different tests as their correct and incorrect answersprompt the computer to take them to different levels. However, the effortin setting up CAT testing is also difficult and learners may not like the factthat they cannot review or change the answers to any questions they havealready answered.210 Build-up 영어교육론ᄆGuideline for Pre-service TeachersCourse 1: A blended language learning courseA language learning course delivered 75 percent online and 25 percentface-to-face. Materials covering the fourskills, grammar and vocabularyare delivered both online and face-to-face, but speaking activities arecarried out mainly face-to-face.Course 2: A face-to-face language learning coursewith additional online materialsA typical language learning course, which uses online tools to supportand extend face-to-face lessons. Strictly speaking, this is not an onlinecourse, but it is the way most teachers get involved in online learningand become more confident with using online tools with their learnersat a distance. The teacher uses the following online tools:- 3 tutor blog to provide extra reading and listening practice, to sethomework and to provide summaries of class work.— Learners email the teacher all class assignments, which are returnedvia e-mail.— The teacher offers regular chat session via Skype for the learners,outside class time, for example every second weekend at a specifictime, for an hour.- The teacher does project work with the class involving ICT tools likeblogs, wikis or podcasts, and encourages learners to work on theseprojects outside class time, in virtual groups.Chapter 04 Computer—assisted Language Learning 21 1Part212Practical English Language Teaching_ 7)ly In the Classroom2012 학년도기출Below is part of an interview of a high school English teacher in charge ofa special program for teaching on- and off-line English writing.1 : What do you think is the most important role of a teacher?T: Well, I think the main job of a teacher is to get students to be able towork on their own. Read the passage and fill in each blank with ONE word.(A) ConcordancingComputers are expert at storing and sorting large amounts of information.Concordancing programs are increasingly being used in the languageclassroom. A concordance is a type of index that searches for occurrencesof a word or combinations of words, affixes, phrases, or structures withina corpus, and can show the immediate context. The output from aconcordance search can be used in the preparation of teaching materials,such as grammar and (1) | | activities.(B) (2) | _ |These are both synchronous and asynchronous in form. They aretypically text-based virtual spaces that rely on the ability of the userto describe environments, and interact with those environments. Bynavigating through space, students create stories in an impromptufashion. They hold dialogs, open boxes, find secret messages, and movethrough cyberspace. Aside from provoking learners to use language inboth planned ways (i.e., writing) and unplanned ways, it also satisfiesthe psychological correlate of searching for information, critical in thelearning process.(2)Chapter 04 Computer—assisted Language Learning 215a,Guideline for Pre-service Teachers QB‘PartPractical English Language Teaching© [4-5] Read the interview and follow the directions.216Below is part of an interview of a high school English teacher in chargeof a special program for teaching on- and off-line English writing.I:T:——What do you think is the most important role of a teacher?Well, I think the main job of a teacher is to get students to be able towork on their own. Practicality평가는 ASA (practical)olojok 한다. 실용적인평가는재정적한계와시간적제약속에서도실시할수있어야 하며, 평가채점및해석이용이한평가를 말한다.An effective test is practical. That means the practical test* is not excessively expensive.* stays within appropriate time constraints.«is relatively easy to administer.- has a scoring/evaluation procedure that is specific and time-efficient.2. Reliability신뢰도있는평가는서로다른상황에서실시해도유사한결과가나오는평가를말한다. 즉신뢰도있는평가는유사한학습자를대상으로다시실시하여도그결과가일관성이있어야 한다.Reliability is defined as the degree to which a test gives consistent anddependable results. Sources of unreliability may lie in the test itself or in thescoring of the test known as test reliability and rater (or scorer) reliability.(1) 채점자 Zt AlZ[&(Inter—rater Reliability)} 의채점자가 WAS 할경우불확실한채점 기준, 선입견, 부주의등에의해서뢰도가낮아질수 있다.oTM= 이평of“Wi=pea220 Build-up SowS= 18&Two or more scorers yield inconsistent scores of the same test, possiblyfor lack of attending to scoring criteria, inexperience, inattention, or evenpreconceived biases.채점자개인 Al@|5(Intra—rater Reliability)한명의채점자가채점을하더라도채점기준이불확실한 경우, 장시간의채점등에의해신뢰도는낮아질수 있다.A common occurrence of low intra-rater reliability results from unclearscoring criteria, fatigue, biases toward particular students, or simplecarelessness.When I am faced with up to 40 tests to grade in only a week, I knowthat the standards I apply-however subliminally-to the first few tests willbe different from those I apply to the last few. I may be ‘easier’ or ‘harder’on those first few papers or I may get tired, and the result may be aninconsistent evaluation across all tests.> 채점자개인의신뢰도를 yo하기전에절반정도를먼저살핀후대략적인채점기준을 Age 후처음부터정기준하에채점을진행할수 있다.. 을16oh4°,12o mtrloo%이내- 오Irea2hRadoga3raw[에=Validity평가의타당도란측정하고자하는 AS 제대로측정하는가를 말한다. 평가가학생들의능력을오차없이측정하였더라도즉 , 신뢰도는높더라도평가항목자체가측정하고자하는언어기능이아니라면평가는평가자에게적절한정보를제공하지 못한다.Validity is defined as the extent to which information you collect actuallyreflects the characteristic or attitude you want to know about. In other words, itexamines whether the instrument is a true reflection of the theory of the traitbeing measured.? Example 1Oral interviewThe scoring analysis for the interview includes several factors in the finalscore; pronunciation, fluency, grammatical accuracy, vocabulary use, andsociolinguistic appropriateness. The justification for these five factors liesin a theoretical construct that claims those factors to be major componentsof oral proficiency. So if you were asked to conduct an oral proficiencyinterview that evaluated only pronunciation and grammar, you could bejustifiably suspicious about the construct validity of that test.<? Example 2Written vocabulary quizLikewise, let’s suppose you have created a simple written vocabularyquiz, covering the content of a recent unit, that asks students to correctlydefine a set of words. Your chosen items may be a perfectly adequatesample of what was covered in the unit, but if the lexical objective ofthe unit was the communicative use of vocabulary.” then the writingof definitions certainly fails to match a construct of communicativelanguage use (Brown, 2004).224 Build-up 영어교육론4) 준거타당도 (<\1161107-01 하 00 Validity)시행된평가결과가동일준거타당도가있다고할수 있다.(01) 공인타당도 (60704[「67[ validity): 현재의평가의결과가기존의타당성을입중받고있는검사와동일한지의여부를의미 한다.(3) OSES (predictive validity) : 어떤평가에서좋은결과를얻은피험자가이와관련된미래의실제생활에서도성공적으로그능하스 있다.eT ^진정성 (&4[76110)목표언어의과업과제시된언어평가과업이일생활에관련된과업을그대로모사하는경우진정성있는 B7치할경우혹은실제상황이나실제a TORalnoe>30,auAuthenticity is defined as the degree of correspondence of the characteristicsof a given language test task to the features of a target language task. It provides the information that washesback to students in the form of useful diagnoses of strengths and weaknesses.? ExampleIn my courses I never give a final examination as the last scheduledclassroom session. 1 always administer a final exam during the penultimatesession, then complete the evaluation of the exams in order to return themto students during the last class. At this time, the students receive scores,grades, and comments on their work, and I spend some of the class sessionaddressing material on which the students were not completely clear. Mysummative assessment is thereby enhanced by some beneficial washbackthat is usually not expected of final examinations.긍정적인역류효과를이끌어내기위한방법1, 내용타당도가높은평가2. 평가전후의전략으로평가전준비와평가결과를다음의학습에반영하도록하는경우평가실시: self-assessment, freer discussion of the test results, journal writing 등? Integrative Test(1) Cloze test@ Definition담화를이룬텍스트의 YRS 비워놓고이를채우게 한다. 빈칸을채우기위해서학습자는빈칸앞뒤의 문맥, 어휘, 문장 구조, 읽기, 선험지식 SS 활용해야하므로대표적인통합평가에 속한다.In cloze test, a sentence with a word left out should be filled witha calculated guess, using linguistic expectancies and background232 Build-up HoseGuideline for Pre-service Teachers 33) ᄒknowledge. Cloze tests are an integrative measure not only of readingability but also other language abilities.@ Types of cloze tests규칙적빈칸 4]-2-7|(fixed—ratio deletion= ᄆ번째의빈칸을규칙적으로비운 다.따라서비워지는단어의품사나문법적기능은예측할수없다 (4616160 inrandom), 이에비해선택적빈칸 4]-2-7| (rational deletion)= 특정품사나문법적기능을하는단어만을의도적으로비운다 .Typically every seventh word is deleted (known as fixed-ratio deletion),but many cloze test designers instead use a rational deletion procedureof choosing deletions according to the grammatical or discourse functionsof the words. Rational deletion also allows the designer to avoid deletingwords that would be difficult to predict from the context.주어진 passageo| 매 nla 어휘를삭제 한다. 작성하기는쉽지만ᄆ째에위치한단어가 reading comprehensiono]] 중요하지않은혹은맥상여러개의답이가능할수있다는단점이 있다.특정학습요소를빈칸으로만드는방법 이다. 예를들면관사에대히focusS = 수업활동인경우관사를빈칸으로 한다. 신뢰도와실용이높지만특정요소만측정한다는한계가 있다.? This alternative eliminates certain problems associated withcloze, such as choice of deletion rate and starting point, representationalsampling of different language elements in the passage, and the inadvertentassessment of written production. Within a C-test, a clue (half the word)serves as a stimulus for respondents to find the other half.? Example 1Pollution is one of the biggest problems in the world today. Alternative Test(1) Characteristics of the alternative assessment@ It requires students to perform, create, produce or do something.@) It uses real-world contexts or simulations.(3) It is non-intrusive in that they extend the day-to-day classroom activities.@ It allows students to be assessed on what they normally do in class everyday.©) It uses tasks that represent meaningful instructional activities.It focuses on processes as well as products.@ It taps into higher-level thinking and problem-solving skills.It provides information about both the strengths and weaknesses ofstudents.(9) It is multi-culturally sensitive when properly administered.It ensures that people, not machines, do the scoring, using humanjudgment.@ It encourages open disclosure of standards and rating criteria.® It calls upon teachers to perform new instructional and assessment roles.236 Build-up SSE 0Guideline for Pre-service Teachers &rus | <Traditional & Alternative AssessmentOne shot, standardized exams Continuous long-term assessmentTimed, multiple-choice format Untimed, free-response formatDecontextualized test items Contextualized communicative tasksScores suffice for feedback Formative, interactive feedbackNorm-referenced scores Criterion-referenced scoresFocus on right answer Open-ended, creative answerSummative FormativeOriented to product Oriented to processFoster extrinsic motivation Foster intrinsic motivationNon-interactive performance Interactive performancerus | x+3247 (performance—based assessment)대부분의대안평가가수행평가를기반으로 한다. My head seemed to be broken. | sometimes feltcold, sometimes hot. | didn’t feel comfortable standing up and | didn’tfeel comfortable sitting down. | hated everything around me. It seemedto me that | got a great pressure from the atmosphere and | couldnot breath. | was so sleepy since | had taken some medicine whichfunctioned as an antibiotic.The room was 50 quiet. | was there by myself and felt very solitary.This dinner reminded me of my mother. whenever | was sick in China, my- mother always took care of me and cooked rice gruel, which has to cookmore than three hours and is very delicious, | think. | would be better verysoon under the care of my mother. But yesterday, | had to cool by myselfeven though | was sick, The more | thought, the less | wanted to eat, Halfan hour passed. The noodles were cold, but | was still sitting there andthinking about my mother. Finally | threw out the noodles and went to bed.Teacher’s response:This is a powerful piece of writing because you really communicatewhat you were feeling. You used vivid details, like “eating tastelessnoodles,” “my head seemed to be broken” and “rice gruel, which has tocook more than three hours and is very delicious.” These make it easyfor the reader to picture exactly what you were going through. Theother strong point about this piece is that you bring the reader fullcircle by beginning and ending with “the noodles.”242 Build-up 영어교육론ᄆGuideline for Pre-service TeachersBeing alone when you are sick is difficult. Now, | know why you were soquiet in class.If you want to another entry related to this one, you could have adialogue with your “sick” self. What would your “healthy” self say to the“sick” self? Is there some advice that could be exchanged about how toprevent illness or how to take care of yourself better when you do getsick? Start the dialogue with your “sick” self speaking first.(Brown, 2004)(3) Self-assessment(A}7 F377 })학습에있어서 student-centered learning®] 중시됨에따라학습자자신에의한학습의평가도중시되고 있다. 교사나채점기준표에의한일방적인평가에서벗어나학생스스로가자신의학습과성취물에대해평가함으로써많은이점을누릴수가 있다. 자가평가는형성평가에서 A 필요한평가방식이며때로는자가평가이외에 peer—assessmentS} 함께사용된 다. 주로 check 116【 를 이용한다.An important means of continuous assessment takes the form of studentself-evaluation. Students are asked to assess themselves each weekaccording to the most appropriate grades listed on a simple form. Thestudents then show their forms at the end of the week and briefly discusstheir results individually with a teacher. Whenever possible, teachers cancompare their own grades with the grades which students have awardedthemselves. Each individual interview will usually take no more than oneor two minutes except in rare cases where there is a great discrepancybetween a student’s self-appraisal and your own view.(a) Advantages of self-assessment자가평가는학생들의학습에대한주체 의식, 선택권, 독립성을키워줌으로써학습에의 autonomyS 높일수 있다. 또한자신에대한성찰을통해만얻거나부족함에대한 ASS 마련함으로써동기를부여할수 있다.‘It allows students to reevaluate the goals they have set forthemselves, to recognize their progress in relation to those goals, andidentify new goals revealed as they progress.Chapter 05 Assessment 243244Practical English Language Teaching* It heightens their awareness of the goals and outcomes of the programand allows them to identify their strengths and need in relation to thoseoutcomes.* It helps them identify how they learn best; reflect on what they can doas learners.It develops a skill common in many workplaces, but that is new formany immigrants.* It gives learners a voice in their education and in shaping the curriculum,they can see themselves as one of the many stakeholders.06) Guidelines for self-assessmentole2z+S-2 self—assessmentS 통해자신의잠재력을파악하고교정적인정보를얻을수 있다. 이러한긍정적인효과를누리기위해 self—assessmentS지도함에있어서주의할 BS 다음과 같다.ᆞ Tell students the purpose of the assessment교사중심의수업과평가에익숙한학생들은자가평가에혼란스러워할수도있다. 자가평가에대한학생들의요구 BAS 바탕으로자가평가에대한올바른개념과목적을알려주어야 한다.« Define the tasks clearly평가를하기전에학생들이수행하는과업에대한안내를명확히하여목적에합당한결과물을가지고평가를하도록 한다. 43 한자가평가를위해교사가a시범을보일수도있으며 check list SS 이용할수 있다,¢ Encourage impartial evaluation of performance or ability자가평가의가장큰한계점은평가에있어서주관성이개입될가능성이크다는점이 다. 이를위해학생들에게객관적이고솔직한평가가주는이점을보여줄필요가 있다.ᆞ Ensure beneficial washback through follow-up tasks자가평가가제공하는 washback 효과를높이기위해서체계적인 follow-up과정이필요 하다. Thistype of scoring emphasizes the task at hand and assigns a score based on theeffectiveness of the text’s achieving that one goal. For example, if the purpose orfunction of an essay is to persuade the reader to do something, the score for thewriting would rise or fall on the accomplishment of that function.분석적채점 AFH (Analytic Scoring Method)학습자들의과제수행을독립적인세부 (하위) GASH 구분해서각각의점수를부여학생들의취약점에따라각영역의비중을조절할수 있다.(9) 학생들에게자신의강점과약점에대한 BRS 제공 한다.@ 하위 SS) 채점자들에게명료한기준을제공하기때문에일관성있고신뢰성이높은채점이가능하다 .단점D 언어능력의종합적인판단에대한정보를제공하지 못한다.@ 총괄적인채점방식에비해타당도가 떨어진다.@ 채점자훈련과채점에시간이많이 걸린다,Chapter 05 Assessment 2471. 문항난이도 (600 Facility)문항난이도는문항이얼마나쉬웠 는지, 즉정답을맞출확률이어느정도인지를 나타낸다.0 과 1 사이에서값이나오며 1 에가까울수록정답률이 높은, 즉쉬운문제 이다.* Item facility C.F.) is an index of how easy an individual item was for thepeople who took it.* It is a number, typically printed as a decimal, ranging from 0.0 to 1.0.* It represents the portion of people who got the item right.LF = 정답자의수0.0 = 모두틀림1.0 = 모두맞음|? Example |2011 학년도기출A high school teacher constructed a 20-item multiple choice Englishtest. She wanted to find out about the test qualities. Read the following and fill in each blank with ONE word.Two approaches are particularly relevant within language testing. (1)| | measurement adopts a framework of comparison betweenindividuals for understanding the significance of any single score.Each score is seen in the light of other scores, particularly in termsof its frequency. (1) || measurement has several advantages. Itallows for distinctions to be made between individual performances.In addition, the procedures for investigating the reliability and validityof scores are well established and well known. However, from aneducational point of view its dependence on comparison across apopulation has been seen as being inappropriately competitive, anddiscouraging for the average student.An alternative approach which does not use a comparison betweenindividuals as its frame of reference is known as (2); | measurement.Here, individual performances are evaluated against a verbal descriptionof a satisfactory performance at a given level. In this way, a series ofperformance goals can be set for individual learners, and they can reachthese at their own rate. As a result, motivation is maintained, and thestriving is for a ‘personal best’ rather than against other learners.[Your answer WMG(2)Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) ※Chapter 05 Assessment 253Practical English Language Teaching03, Read the passage and follow the directions.254| Your answer |English teachers are looking for a standardized test. [2 points]| Your answer @p (2)In comprehending aural language listeners do a great deal of constructiveand interpretative work in which they integrate what they hear with whatthey know about the world. According to one view, the listeners segmentthe stream of speech into its constituent sounds, link these together to formwords, chain the words together to form clauses and sentences and soon. This view is known as the | (1) | approach to listening. On theother hand, the listeners can bring knowledge from outside the text to thetask of interpreting and comprehending the text itself. Successful listenersand readers are those who can utilize both ‘inside the head’ knowledgeand ‘outside the head’ knowledge to interpret what they hear and see. Theuse of inside the head knowledge, that is, knowledge which is not directlyencoded in words, is known as the | (2) | view of listening.(1) In the Grammar Translation Method and Audiolingual Method,formal aspects of language received central attention. In the DirectMethod and Natural Approach, overt focus on form was almostforbidden. Some manifestations of CLT especially indirect approachesadvocated only a passing attention to form, while other proponentsof CLT injected healthy doses of form-focused techniques into acommunicative curriculum.(2) Grammatical consciousness-raising (CR) is an approach to theteaching of grammar in which instruction in grammar is viewed as away of raising the learner’s awareness of grammatical features of thelanguage. This CR approach is contrasted with traditional approachesto the teaching of grammar.Chapter 01 기출변형문제 263Guideline for Pre-service Teachers @1999 학년도ro264Based on two assumptions, the characteristics of GCR(GrammaticalConsciousness Raising) are given as follows:A_ «CR takes the view that form is best learnt when the learner's focus is| on meaning.ᆞ @ rejects the split between the conscious learning and subconsciousacquisition.| * CR pays great attention to the form-function relationship.자 ...Write three characteristics of CR using the couples of key concepts below,referring to the sentence structures from <A>.* grammatical structures — the communicative context* fluency — accuracy* linear view — organic view0(2)(3)Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 33)05. Read the following passages. [4 points] 2002 하년[A] Knowing vocabulary is important for getting the meaning from atext. L2 readers frequently say that they need more vocabulary, sothat they can understand the meaning of a sentence. Understandingthe basics of grammatical structure enables readers to understandthe relationship between words, but it does not provide access tothe meaning of the sentence, Knowing the meaning of each contentword does.[B] For many of us, our perspective on teaching vocabulary was greatlyinfluenced by the top-down, naturalistic, and communicativeapproaches of the 1970s and 1980s. The emphasis was implicit,incidental learning of vocabulary. We were taught the importanceof directing L2 students to recognize clues in context, to usemonolingual dictionaries, and to avoid defining words or glossingtexts with their bilingual equivalents. Textbook emphasized inferringword meaning from context as the primary vocabulary skill.Exposure to a word in a variety of context is extremely important forunderstanding the depth of the word’s meaning.[C] Some research points to the ineffectiveness of using implicitvocabulary instruction and the need for a much stronger wordlevel or bottom-up approach that had been previously advocated.It argues that explicit vocabulary instruction has an effect onstudents’overall interest and motivation in learning words, whichmay in turn explain how students receiving explicit instructionhave improved comprehension of tests. some techniques of explicitvocabulary instruction include dictionary work, word unit analysis,mnemonic devices, semantic elaboration, and oral production.266 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre~service Teachers 2)Fill in each blank of the following summary. Read the following passage and answer the question. [3 points]The features of real-world listening input include the use of time-creating, facilitation, and compensation devices. To ease the productionof speech, the speaker normally uses time-creating devices. These areused to gain time for the speaker so that he can formulate what to saynext in spontaneous speech. One typical example is the use of pausefillers. Despite the lack of syntactic or lexical functions that pause fillersserve, they help the speaker to solicit more time to plan and in turn tofurnish the listener with more processing time.The pressure of time in real-life communication also renders itnecessary for the speaker to use facilitation devices to ease speechproduction. Effective listeners need to identify and be familiar withthese devices in free speech. The use of less complex structures is oneof these devices. Formulaic language use is another device to facilitatespeech production. These devices will normally give the impression offluency; they serve the function of filling unwanted pauses. As effectivelisteners, students need to understand their function.Due to the speed of natural speech, listening input has to beprocessed very quickly. Fortunately, redundancy in natural speechdoes allow the listener some processing time. The three typical waysto build in redundancy are repetition, reformation, and rephrasing.Speakers always find themselves correcting or improving what theyhave already said. They may repeat part of the speech or express theirideas in a different way. This kind of redundancy is necessary to helpunderstanding on the part of the listener. Effective listeners thereforeidentify these elements of redundancy and are able to guess meaningswith the help of compensation devices.Based on information from the passage, complete the following sentenceusing ALL AND ONLY the words in the box. The word ‘the’ can be usedmore than once.272 = Build-up 영어교육론12.| Your answer |Read the following passage and answer the question. Norm-referenced measurement adopts a framework of comparison betweenindividuals for understanding the significance of any single score. Eachscore is seen in the light of other scores, particularly in terms of itsfrequency. Norm-referenced measurement has several advantages. Itallows for (1) . In addition, the procedures for investigatingthe reliability and validity of scores are well established and wellknown. However, from an educational point of view its dependence oncomparison across a population has been seen as being inappropriatelycompetitive, and discouraging for the average student.An alternative approach which does not use a comparison betweenindividuals as its frame of reference is known as criterion-referencedmeasurement. Here, individual performances.are evaluated against averbal description of a satisfactory performance at a given level. In thisway, a series of performance goals can be set for individual learners,and they can reach these at their own rate. Read the comments about the errors above and fill in the blank with| Your answer |14, Read the passage and follow the directions. [2 points]uideline for Pre-service Teachersone suitable term. [2 points]In English, as in other languages, there are many fixed, identifiable, non-idiomatic phrases and constructions. Such groups of words are called fixedcombinations or collocations. Research findings suggest that collocationalerrors take place with expressions for which there is no direct translationalequivalence between English and the learners’ mother tongue. Giventhis research result, the probable source of the errors in the e-mail is| |in the course of language development.When mothers speak to their children, they typically simplify their speechand make efforts to sustain communication. The formal and interactionalcharacteristics of this kind of speech are referred to as “motherese.” Theymay help the child to learn the language. When native speakers addresslearners, they adjust their normal speech in order to facilitate understanding.These adjustments, which involve both language form and languagefunction, constitute foreigner talk. Foreigner talk may aid acquisition byensuring that the learner understands what he or she hears. Foreigner talkclosely resembles motherese, but there are notable differences in both inputand interactional features. Generally, ungrammatical adjustments are veryrare in motherese, but they can occur under certain conditions in foreignertalk. Whereas motherese displays a high proportion of instructions andquestions, foreigner talk has a higher proportion of statements.Chapter 01 기출변형문제 2752005 학년도15. [3 points] 2006 하년도rMultiple-choice questions are often constructed in a way that makes itdifficult to have valid score interpretation. Consider the item below.Choose the one word that best completes thesentence.Charlie is always late for school, so his motheris going to buy an — clock for him.(a) ring | 06) alarm© morning @ bell:In the example above, the item writer intended to find out whetherthe test taker knows the meaning of ‘alarm’ and whether he or sheknows this word best fits the context semantically. [4 points]0)개NNS : I go cinema.NS: Uh?NNS : I go cinema last night.NS: Oh, last night.The Interaction Hypothesis suggests a number of ways in whichinteraction can contribute to language acquisition. More specifically,it suggests that (a) when interactional modifications lead tocomprehensible input via the decomposition and segmenting of input,acquisition is facilitated; that (b) when learners receive feedback,acquisition is facilitated; and that (c) when learners are pushed toreformulate their own utterances, acquisition is promoted.The above dialogue shows that the interaction has led to successfulcommunication, but that it does not contribute to the | (1) | of thepast tense, a morphological feature. Thesame word should be used only once.The goal of input-processing instruction is to encourage learners tomake better form-meaning connections than they would if left to theirown devices. There are three key components. As in the worksheetabove, for example, they are encouraged to match pictures with bold-typed forms which carry the active and passive voice. In other words,a form-meaning relationship in the picture explains the use of thepassive to (1) the patient of a sentence by placing it in subjectposition. Secondly, the picture leads them to attend to the form of theverb to determine whether the subject is the agent of the verb, as ismost generally the case, or the patient, as is the case with passive verbs.Finally, the worksheet represents a structured-input activity wherelearners have the chance to process the targeted feature in a controlledmanner. Unlike the traditional grammar instruction, this activity isdesigned to help learners naturally process | (2) _in accordance |with their interlanguage.Chapter 01 기출변형문제 28322.284Jo Word List (eerecover input topicalize output ignore feedback| Your answer [6D (2)Read the following passage and fill in each blank with one appropriateword from the word list below it. Read the following and fill in the blanks with a suitable word from a box.2008 학년도&25. Fill in the blank with all and only the words from the word list in the correctorder. You can use the word the more than once. [4 points]A development in teaching listening has been the increased use ofauthentic materials. Recordings of spontaneous speech expose learnersto the rhythms of natural everyday English in a way that scriptedmaterials cannot, however good the actors. Furthermore, authenticpassages where the language has not been graded to reflect thelearners’ level of English afford a listening experience much closer toa real-life one. It is vital that students of a language be given practicein dealing with texts where they understand only part of what is said.For these two reasons, it is advisable to introduce authentic materialsearly on in a language course. In general, students are not daunted ordiscouraged by authentic materials—provided they are told in advancenot to expect to understand everything. Indeed, they find it motivatingto discover that they can extract information from an ungraded passage.The essence of this approach is as follows: Instead of simplifying thelanguage of the text, | . With a text above the language levelof the class, one demands only shallow comprehension. One mightplay a recording of a real-life stall holder in a market and simply ask theclass to write down all the vegetables that are mentioned.cower Word List 이 0 20220the of that demandedis task simplify student2008 학년도Chapter 01 기출변형문제 287ee형및영역별문제26. Read the followings <A> and <B> and fill in the blanks in <B> with the288words from <A>. [4 points]AThe classroom conversation below is an example of proceduralvocabulary at work. The declarative knowledge or meaning beingasserted is ‘anesthetic.’ The procedural words used to break this downinclude put, someone, make, them, and so on.Teacher : And some drugs can also be used as anesthetics, like...Student : What is anesthetic?Teacher : Oh er... when you put someone to sleep, you make them goto sleep before an operation.Student : Sleep?Teacher : Yes, you anesthetize them... you give them a drug or anestheticthat makes them sleep... so they have no pain... you make themsleepy.BThe acquisition of the meaning of the word anesthetic is negotiatedthrough the use of procedural vocabulary. Therefore, students need to betaught how to use| (1) | vocabulary in order to effectively learn the| (2) | vocabulary. Communicative competence includes not only2 the idealized | (2) | knowledge we have of word meaning, but the(1) | knowledge we draw on in converting that knowledge toperformance.| Your answer Gy (2)Build-up 영어교육론 II2008 학년도27.An optimal scenario for development, and hence internalization, isthe zone of proximal development (ZPD). In other words, an essentialfeature of learning is that it creates the zone of proximal development;that is, learning awakens a variety of internal developmental processesthat are able to operate only when the child is interacting with peoplein his or her environment and in cooperation with peers. Oncethese processes are internalized, they become part of the child’sdevelopmental achievement.One way of conceptualizing movement within the ZPD is the stagesof regulation, or control over intellectual actions. It has been proposedthat, in the transition from interpsychological to intrapsychologicalactivity, the learner moves from other-regulation to complete self-regulation. When other-regulated, the learner can perform withassistance from others. The learner achieves self-regulation when, inthe course of ZPD interactional processes, he or she can take control ofexternal actions and is capable of independent problem solving. In theabsence of other-regulation or when not responding to other-regulation,the learner may be at a stage of object-regulation, a stage in which thelearner is easily regulated by objects in the environment.Because assistance in the ZPD is extended as long 85 || persistsbut is removed once the learner can function independently, it hasbeen metaphorically conceived as a form of scaffolding. Traditionally,the concept of scaffolding has referred to the supportive behaviors bywhich an expert can help a novice learner achieve higher levels ofregulation.Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) =Read the following and fill in the blank with the word from the passage.2008 학년도| Your answer |Chapter 01 기출변형문제 289Part28. Read the passage and answer the questions. [5 points] 20028[ 노도iMultimedia applications are helping teachers to teach foreignlanguages regardless of learning style or pace. CD-ROM titles arebeing used to present information in multiple forms that can bepersonalized far more easily than paper methods. In teaching listeningcomprehension to students in class, for instance, many schoolspreviously relied on videotapes of movies and a large stack of printedmaterials. Some students did well with these resources, others, lessmotivated, got bogged down in the dense texts.With web technology, the school now restructures a series of teachingasks according to complexity. Students are required to complete acertain amount of work to ensure that they understand the concept.The listening comprehension task incorporates multimedia animation ofmoving objects to help every student understand both the meaning ofthem and their related language expressions. The most advanced taskinvolves a web search where students are asked to fill in a worksheet,while they are surfing the web. Students often explore the web sitesfurther in order to find out information which the teacher asks them tosearch.Multimedia applications can help teachers change the teaching stylefrom the traditional approach-a teacher talking at the front of theclassroom, coupled with listening comprehension assignments-to amore hands-on approach that takes advantage of the natural curiosityof students of all ages. Multimedia applications enable students toexplore information through the web sites, to model experiments, andto collaborate with one another.Chapter 01 기출변형문제 _ 295Part1-1. [5 points]2003 학년도Purpose: To provide students with an opportunity to share privately inwriting their reaction, questions, and concerns about school experienceswith the teacher without any threat of reprisal or evaluation.Rationale: The notion of these strategies is a partial refinement ofjournal writing. Their major characteristic is the importance given tocommunications between the student and the teacher. They provide theteacher with the opportunity not only to learn what students are thinkingand doing but also to share thoughts and suggestions with them.Often journals were used to encourage diarylike entries of what tookplace in the way of progress on a project; sometimes they were usedto give students the opportunity to respond freely to what took place atschool or home, or to respond to a book or some other forms of literature.While the teacher might not respond to every entry, the intent of thisactivity is to have students write to the teacher and to have the teacherwrite a genuine response to the student. The teacher does not evaluatethe student’s comments as either right or wrong. What is important tonote is the teacher’s respect for the privacy of the journal as well as thenonjudgmental and nonprescriptive nature of the teacher’s reaction.Discussions to be made are left up to the student.Intended Audience: can be used with students of 9th grade and overin Korea.Chapter 01 기출변형문제 __297Part기출변형및 SSS 문제iin Ge aes SAPS ST3-1. [4 points]2004 학년도The class has 30 EFL students at an intermediate level of proficiency.They meet four times a week for 50 minutes each class.Step 1: The teacher has the students divide into groups of five. Sincethere are thirty students, that creates six groups of five students.Step 2: One member of each group is given a picture strip story. Thereare six pictures in a row on a piece of paper, but no words. Thepictures tell a story.Step 3: The student with the story shows the first picture to the othermembers of his or her group, while covering the remainingfive pictures. Less than 15 words should be used in each case. [3 points]2004 학년도Some pre-reading activities have tended to focus exclusively on preparingthe readers for likely linguistic difficulties in a text. More recently, attentionhas shifted to cultural or conceptual difficulties. However, pre-readingactivities may not just offer compensation for second language readers’supposed linguistic or sociocultural inadequacies. In fact, they may alsoremind readers of what they already know and think, that is, activateexisting schematic knowledge.(1) What do you think?Think about your best friend. Read the passage and follow the directions. [4 points] 2006 학년도If we think of a mixed class as being mixed in language skills and levels,age, academic background, mother tongue, sex, personality, languageaptitude, learning style and other factors, then really every class we teachis mixed. It is strange that we tend to regard heterogeneous classes as aspecial category when they are our everyday reality.There are in fact many advantages to teaching heterogeneous classes.They are interesting because of the sheer richness of their human resources.They are often bursting with energy precisely because of all the differencesthey contain. They give scope for peer teaching too.Such mixed classes do, however, have some drawbacks. It is difficult tomeet all the widely differing expectations held by individual students. It isalso difficult to make sure that everyone in the classroom learns. It is trickyto find materials, activities, topics and a pace to suit most participants.Those who are not catered for can soon become disaffected or bored.Thus, planning for heterogeneous classes will be very important.Referring to the passage above, write the benefits and drawbacks inheterogeneous class.| Your answer |(1) Benefits:(2) Drawbacks:Chapter 01 기출변형문제 _ 307Part© [9-10] Read the passage and follow the directions.Using authentic materials is one of the main stays of an imaginative andmotivating higher level course, but rarely features at levels lower thanintermediate. There are several reasons for this. One is a kind of fear thatstudents will panic when faced with language that is largely unfamiliar. Thereis a feeling that, to prevent students from panicking, the language should beedited to the students’ level. This is an unnecessary fear, as using authenticmaterials can be rewarding and stimulating for both teachers and students.Authentic materials are linguistically difficult, but that’s not the point. It istrue that authentic materials, written or recorded, are likely to be too hard evenfor advanced students. The trick, regardless of the materials used, is not toedit and grade the materials, but to develop and use a variety of tasks that suityour students’ abilities. Especially with lower levels, it needs to be emphasizedthat students don’t have to understand everything in order to perform the settasks. Students often don’t believe you until you go through a few tasks withthem. By helping students conquer authentic materials with a variety of tasks,you come to build their confidence in coping with the unknown, an importantelement in their development as independent learners. |09. This lesson helps learners engage in completing tasks collaboratively. Also, it다integrates language skills across the two task cycles. Furthermore, it provideslearners with opportunities for planned production. Finally, it winds down withwork on specific language features.2301. Spoken language contains a good deal of reduced forms and sentence segments020305.which can make the listening process difficult. These forms involves unstressedvowels, omitted sounds and other alternations of the full form, such as assimilation,contraction, and blending. For example, there are as follows: “Dijeeyet?” for “Didyou eat yet?”, “Whaddaya?” for “what do you do or what are you?” and “whatcha”for “what have you”.Second language learning is a process of the creative construction of a target languagesystem. By trial and error and hypothesis testing, learners establish interlanguage, whichhas a structurally intermediate status between the native and target languages. It is ownunique and coherent internalized rule system, which rarely becomes totally congruentwith the target language system. Therefore, learning language fundamentally involvesthe making of errors, which may be a sign of progress. In a language classroom, mostteachers should consider errors as a part of learning. Furthermore, they should helplearners to notice their linguistic output in class, and slowly convert systematic errorsinto appropriate form by giving feedback.Information gap is a useful communicative activity, which one person has informationthat the other lacks. During the activity, students should use the target languageto share that information. By conveying and requesting the information they areengaged in communicative interaction (negotiation for meaning) that results indeveloping their communicative competence.Question Type B is more authentic and communicative than Question Type A. Asa primary reason, the former is questions to which we do not know the answer.Accordingly, it requests real information, which leads conversation betweenparticipants to negotiate meaning. The latter, on the other hand, is questions towhich we know the answer. Such a question, for example, when we hold up abook and ask, “Is this a book?” is used for checking one’s linguistic knowledge ina language classroom.Episode Hypothesis states that the text will be easier to reproduce, understand, andrecall to the extent that it is motivated and structured episodically. According to thisview, Conversation <B> is the most effective material in that it captivates learners’interest through its episodic organization. In the first place, Conversation B gripslearners with suspense by provoking their expectation “what’s going to happennext?” Second, it has a familiar setting and ordinary characters. Third, because theoutcome Cif Chrissy is back home or not) is not clear, they are apt to be involvedin the content. Fourth, it facilitates the interaction of cognition and language withlogically or episodically sequenced sentences. Finally, since it shows universal storylearners easily identify with the characters.Chapter 01 기출변형문제 345Guideline for Pre-service Teachers ig) "oo06. 6-1. The three students in the above have complaints about their speaking classesas follows: First off, Min-su thinks that lots of drills and practices prevent himfrom improving his speaking ability. Next, Homin wants his teacher to givefeedback, at least, on his major errors, which, otherwise, would be likely to befossilized. Finally, Sujin complains that the speaking activities in class do notcorrelate closely with course assessment she should take, which demotivatesher in class.6-2. For Minsu and Homin, “the information exchange task” with its follow-uptreatment is recommendable, where it requires participants to exchange theirreal information and to focus on the language they used during the task.Supposing the task is to exchange students’daily routines, here, Min-su canget natural opportunity to talk about real things for his oral competence. ForHomin, on the other hand, as he reflects what he talked about and gets somefeedback on his mistakes in the follow-up treatment, he does not have toworry about the language accuracy.6-3. In terms of washback effect, for Sujin, the teacher should prepare a regularoral test, which is closely related to course content and, also, increase speakingpercentage of whole score. Furthermore, through interactive feedback heshould inform Su-jin of her strength and weakness in speaking.07. 7-1, Here, Ms. Lee and Mr. Kim shows different writing approaches. In the case of346Ms. Lee she takes a product-oriented writing approach which focuses on the finalproduct, the coherent, error-free text. Mr. Kim, on the other hand, recommendsa process-oriented writing approach as an alternative. This alternative approachfocuses on process(steps) involved in drafting and redrafting a piece of workrather than a final product. Unlike Ms. Lee’s writing approach, in addition, byplacing central importance on the process of revision, the alternative helps studentwriters to be involved in interactive writing work.7-2. The Natural Order Hypothesis assumes that target items or rules are acquiredaccording to not instructional but developmental sequences. Accordingly, Ms.Lee, who does not respect the fact, corrects in vain her students’ errors ongrammatical items that they are not yet ready to acquire.7-3, Social constructivism assumes that social interaction can facilitate languageacquisition. According to this view, a process-oriented writing task can besuggested, where students work in pairs and groups to generate ideas and topeer-edit as an interactive and sharing process.Build-up 영어교육론 11Rekiifmeat08. 8—1, This essay has strong and weak points in terms of content and organization. Withregard to the content, as a strong point, the writer provides abundant examplesrelated to the topic by mentioning temperature, clothing, outdoor activities, andfeelings. Here, he or she elaborates the reason why he likes summer by “Thetemperature is good for me”, (or “I like the summer clothing and the outdooractivities”, and “I am never bored during a summer”.) The weak point, on the otherhand, is that the writer provides information, unrelated to the topic. For example,the sentence “I have bought a heavy coat on sale from the department storeyesterday” violates the principle of the coherence. In terms of the organization,its merit lies in that it follows the format of “introduction-body-conclusion”. In theessay, the topic sentence “Summer is my favorite season” is presented at first, andthe supporting details are followed. At the end of the writing, the conclusion isgiven. The writer, however, does not use appropriate conjunction or transitionalwords. For instance, before the sentence “Sometimes I don’t like the hot weatherbecause it make me uncomfortable”, the adversative conjunction like “however” isneeded to connect two contrasting ideas, but there is no conjunction at all. Thus,it violates the cohesion of the writing.8-2. To use correction symbols when giving feedback has both advantages anddisadvantages. In the first place, correction symbols indicate where an erroris and what type of error it is. Accordingly, with the information studentsare encouraged to self-correct their errors. Next, since they are simple touse, teachers can give feedback with less effort in a relatively short time.However, there are disadvantages in using correction symbols. One is thatcorrection symbols can often be inappropriate to point out every error. Inparticular, when students make contextual or discourse errors, these couldnot be indicated with simple symbols. The other disadvantage is that studentsmay not know what the correct form is even if they are informed of the errortype.09. 9-1. When Mr. Kang uses English with his students, he modifies his languageto facilitate communication depending on students’ proficiency level. Inparticular, with low-level students, it would clearly be of little benefit for himto speak quickly and use idiomatic language. Thus, he adjusts his language,both in form and function, so that the students can understand more easily andactively participate in the classroom activities.Chapter 01 기출변형문제 _ 3479-2,His talk in the advanced and Intermediate-low levels is differentiated in threeways. First off, he shows adaptation of syntax in he uses less complex languagewith intermediate-low level students. For example, he divides complex sentence“Suppose that someone broke into your apartment and you found your laptop wasmissing.” into simpler four sentences like “Imagine this. Someone broke into yourapartment. You couldn't find your computer. It was gone!” Next, as adaptationof vocabulary, he chooses more frequent vocabulary items for his intermediate-low levelled students. For instance, he uses “built” instead of “constructed”, and“long ago” instead of “in ancient times” for the low-level students. Finally, the lastunderlined part shows conceptual adaptation. For the advanced level students,he uses metalinguistic terms such as “active sentences” and “passive sentences”without any explicit explanation. With the intermediate-low level students, on theother hand, he presents today’s concept more explicitly and logically by providingconcrete examples of active and passive sentence like “People built the pyramidslong ago” and “The pyramids were built long ago”.. There are five ways that Mr. Kang differentiates task complexity in thesetwo classes. First off, in Step 1, less cognitive processing is demanded tothe low-level students by changing speed, and writing down words only.Second, task is simplified in step 2. That is, while he requires the advancedstudents to reconstruct the text, he wants intermediate-low level students tomake sentences. Third, in terms of grammatical awareness, the advanced levelstudents are to focus on meaning and form while the intermediate-low levelstudents focus on meaning only. Fourth, the advanced level students evaluatetheir products holistically in terms of content and form while the intermediate-low level students check the target item (the passive form) only. Finally, interms of task outcome, the advanced level students are required to presentthe outcome (oral production) while the intermediate-low level students areasked to rewrite the text without oral response.10. 10-1. Ms. Park’s initial scoring rubric in <Table 1>, which evaluates only two factors,34810-2.pronunciation and grammatical accuracy, results in low construct validityin that the scoring analysis for oral proficiency should include several sub-measurements in the final scale like pronunciation, grammatical accuracy,fluency, vocabulary and cohesion.Accordingly, Ms. Park’s initial scoring rubric in <Table 1> leads us to makeerror in judgement about Jitae and Mina’s oral performance level. That is,although they have different levelled oral proficiency in terms of moredetailed sub-measurement, it cannot make a discrimination about their oralperformance.Build-up 영어교육론 110-3.11.11~1.11-2.GuThe missing ratings for Jitae and Mina can be given as follows. [ 기입형 ]358AIn an English class, students who start by saying be went, they came, etc.suddenly start saying he goed and they comed. What seems to be happening inthat the students start to apply a new rule that has been subconsciouslylearnt, and, as a result, even make mistakes with things that theyseemed to have known before. Later, however, it all gets sorted out asthe students begin to have a more sophisticated understanding, andthey go back to saying went and came while, at the same time, handlingregular past tense endings. Also, they make the same kind of errors aswell. This accounts for mistakes like *She is more nicer than him wherethe acquisition of more for comparatives is applied and then mixed upwith the rule that the students have learnt—that comparative adjectiveare formed with an adjective + er.The students overgeneralize rules of regular past tense and comparativeadjective into irregular category. Here, this phenomenon of movingfrom a correct form to an incorrect form shown in <A> is referred to as| (1) |. Also, These students seem to go through backsliding indeveloping English language system. To learn these exceptions to therules in <A> the | (2) | strategy could be recommended.Fill in the blanks with appropriate terms using TWO words.[Your answer 불안(2)Build-up S22 1MeGuideline for Pre-service Teachers08. Read the following <A> and its teaching implication in <B>. Answer thequestion. [서술형]AThe effect of age on second language acquisition has been extensivelydocumented, the issue being whether younger learners acquire a secondlanguage more efficiently and effectively than older learners. Researchto date has not conclusively settled the issue of age one way or another,largely because the issue is more complex than it might seem at first.In order to investigate this issue, it is necessary to distinguish betweenthe effect of age on the route of acquisition, the rate, and ultimateattainment. Reviews of the available literature concluded that, while agedoes not alter the route of acquisition, it does have a marked effect onthe rate and ultimate success.BAs shown above, the research argues that the starting age normallyaffect how rapidly the learners acquire the language. Also, youngerlearners are likely to end up being more proficient than older learners.Generally, however, the same target language items are acquired inthe same order at which learners areexposed to the target language for the first time.Based on the passage, complete the summary in <B> using FOUR words.Chapter 02 영역별문제 __36718.368OU esRead the following learning logs students wrote after their Englishconversation classes. Children usually focus on meaning rather than on form. Accordingly, they do notimitate the target form simply.02. + Similiarities:In both <A> and <B>, NNS receives feedback about its lack of comprehensibilityin the form of a clarification request. In addition, both of NNSs are pushed toreformulate his initial utterance.ᆞ Differences:NNS in <B> modifies his linguistic output by reformulating the utterance in amore target-like way. NNS in <A>, however, does not modify previous utterancesince she sees NS’s the second feedback as positive evidence.03. scaffolding04. Passage <A> assumes that Korean students will have difficulty learning Englishbecause of the interference of the Korean language system with the Englishlanguage system. As mentioned above, for example, Korean students do not drawa distinction between two sounds, /1/ and /r/ in English language. This difficulty iscaused by that the sound /@/ in Korean Language is converted into two sounds,/1/ and /r/ in English Language.05. interlanguage06. One is that the learner language of the student is at the systematic stage, notemergent one. The other is that the teacher wants to communicate with the studentthrough referential question, not display one.07. (1) U-shaped learning (2) garden path08. explicit correction09. other-initiated other repair10. circumlocution11. Contrastive Analysis12. (1) repetitive drills (2) inductive |13. Student 1 belongs to systematic developmental stage of interlanguage because shecan correct her error, following the teacher’s feedback. (the uptake of Student 1follows the teacher’s feedback.)14. Here, either of students arrived at the correct collocation through the verbalcollaboration of peers, called scaffolding. This enabled them to use the targetlanguage form at a level beyond their present competence.15. (1) confirmation check (2) clarification request (3) recastChapter 02 SAH Sal 38516. Two of the main causes of English errors the Korean student made are as follows:interlingual (interference) and intralingual (developmental) factors. First off, hemade an intralingual error by using ‘the’ with a place name. This is evidence thathe is learning to use articles in front of nouns but has not yet learned that they donot occur before most place names. Next, he produced an interference error bymissing English verb ‘was’. In other words, since the word for ‘warm’ in Korean isa verb itself, here, he did not use an additional verb ‘was’.17. regardless of the age18. For Hyun-ji she is intrinsically motivated and a high risk-taker. Mi-sun, on the otherhand, uses metacognitive strategies as a reflective learner.19. @ rules/principles 06) central message/main idea/gist20. (1) code-switching (2) avoidance21. Owing to insufficient knowledge of intercultural difference, both of them seemto go through the culture shock, which is a feeling of discomfort and fear comingfrom different culture. For example, here, they take different views of keepingsilent. For the Korean student he kept silent out of respect. His British teacher,however, took this as a refusal to answer the question.[Another examples](1) The Korean student looked down to be respectful, instead of looking directly atthe teacher’s face. The teacher, however, considered this as a sign that he wasnot paying attention.(2) The Korean student smiled as a sign of being sorry to the teacher at a time whena British person would never do so. His smile was misinterpreted by the teacher,who thought the student was being less than serious.22. (1) display (2) initiation(3) response (4) evaluation23. The student’s errors are not amenable to self-repair, and the student is notdevelopmentally ready to acquire the form.24. In <A>, the teacher plays the role of director (controller, ringmaster). He asksdisplay questions. The teacher in <B>, on the other hand, as a scaffolder, (resourceperson) or facilitator gives referential questions and helps the learner struggle toexpress herself.25. <A> : Since the student’s utterance in <A> contains an error of form, the teacher386reformulates her production accurately by changing Mary into Mary’s, the form ofthe possessive.<B> : Since meaning is problem in <B>, the teacher recasts inappropriate phrasalverb, look at, in a better form, look up, for what the student means to say.Build-up 영어교육론그26. (1) circumlocution (2) circumlocution(3) mime (noverbal strategy) (4) message abandonment (avoidance)27. ᆞ). Lee : Mr. Lee supports Contrastive Analysis Hypothesis which assumes theefrors occurs as a result of interference of the first language system into the second.In her view, thus, students’ errors should be prevented as the failure of languagelearning.« Ms. Shin : Ms. Shin follows Error Analysis which identifies and explains errors.Assuming that making errors is a part of learning, she considers errors as indicatorof what problem her students have in learning English.28. the first language29.A:c,e | B:bC:d,g D:a,f30. (1) instrumentally (2) facilitative31. Both <A> and <B> sequences are typical of teacher-student exchanges in the 12classroom. However, Classroom Talk <B> is more authentic and communicativeclassroom exchange rather than <A>. To be more specific, in <B> the teacherinvites students to share student’s personal experience and thereby to move theconversation forward. The teacher in <A>, on the other hand, closes down theinteraction in the third move by providing an evaluation, which disrupts thecommunicative flow of classroom discourse.Next, the collaborative dialogue, another alternative of the Classroom Talk in <A>,entails scaffolded learning. In this process, the teacher or other more advancedpeers provide supports, or scaffolds, to assist learners in acquiring and producingnew aspects of the language, often modeling for them the desired outcome. Asthey become more autonomous in their production of the target language, thesescaffolds are gradually removed. Accordingly, through this dialogue, the teacherbuilds in opportunities for the learners to notice new language features andencourages them to practice using these features.32. Sumi is very extroverted in that she likes to be around other people and dislikesbeing alone. Kang-min, on the other hand, is somewhat introverted because hedoes not need other people as much and prefers to be on his own.33. The student’s learnt knowledge is not transferred to acquisition.Chapter 02 영역별문제 _ 3.87ICT Classroom01. Read the following and answer the question. [7/2/34]Communicative Language Teaching (CLT) is not a monolithic anduniform approach. It has been acknowledged that there are twoversions of CLT, namely the weak and the strong version. The formeris based on the assumptions that the components of communicativecompetence can be identified and systematically taught. In this respect,a weak version of CLT does not involve a radical departure from_ earlier methods as it reflects what has been referred to as a TypeA approach to language teaching, i.e. an approach that is analytic(interventionist). Thus, instead of (or, perhaps in addition to) teachinglearners the structural properties of language, a weak version of. CLTproposes they be taught how to realize specific general conceptssuch as ‘duration’ and ‘possibility’, and language functions such as‘inviting’ and ‘apologizing’. The weak version of CLT is manifest in theproposals for | (1) . In contrast, a strong versions of CLT claimsthat ‘language is acquired through communication’. That is, learnersdo not first acquire language as a structural system and then learn howto use this system in communication but rather actually discover thesystem itself in the process of learning how to communicate. The strongversion of CLT, therefore, involves providing learners with opportunitiesto experience how language is used in communication. This approachreflects what has been called a Type B approach, i.e. an approach thatis holistic(non-interventionist). It is evident in | (2) | and also inproposals for teaching centered on the use of task.Fill in the blanks with TWO or THREE words./Youranswer 불안(2)388 Build-up 영어교육론02. Such tasks can beplaced on a continuum from rehearsal tasks to activation tasks.Rehearsal task is a piece of classroom work in which learnersrehearse, in class, a communicative act they will carry out outside of theclass. It bears a clear and obvious relationship to its corresponding real-world counterpart.Activation task is a piece of classroom work involving communicativeinteraction, but NOT one in which learners will be rehearsing for someout-of-class communication. Rather they are designed to activate theacquisition process.Real-world or target task is a communicative act we achieve throughlanguage in the world outside the classroom.8 SEE 여고 ROLY “ae He CLReferring to <C>, identify the task type of <A> and <B> respectively withits rationale.
